Survey of Wasteland in Twenty Provinces

(Nanjing) Internal news: Gansu held a survey of wasteland last year. The total amount of wasteland in 26 counties, including Weiyuan, was 13,116,593 mu, of which less than 8% was cultivated. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

International Labor Conference; Two Proposals from China Decided

(Nanjing) Tang Jianfei, Director of the Labor Department of the Ministry of Industries, said that the employer and worker representatives from China attending the International Labor Conference will be selected and decided. After the list is sent to the Ministry, it will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. They will set sail around the end of next month. Two proposals from China have been decided: 1. The Contract Labor Case; 2. The issue of youth unemployment. Relevant materials are being collected, compiled, and completed, and will be handed over to the employer and labor representatives to take with them. (Special Dispatch, 23rd)

Ministry of Industries Plans to Establish Employment Agency

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industries plans to establish an employment agency and has drafted regulations, which have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for transfer to the Legislative Yuan for review. (Special Dispatch, 23rd)

Jiangsu Anti-Smoking Association Holds Meeting Yesterday

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Anti-Smoking Committee resolved on the 23rd: (1) Recommend Ye Chucang to give a scheduled anti-smoking speech on the Central Broadcasting Station; (2) Recommend Ye Chucang to hire Zhou Fohai and Cheng Tianfang as judges for the student anti-smoking speech contest; (3) Increase the number of full-time auditors in each county as needed; (4) Smokers who do not attend the anti-smoking lectures will be detained and forced to quit smoking, and then given a detention sentence. (Central News Agency, 23rd)

Wang Kemin Goes South to Visit Huang Fu

(Beiping) Wang Kemin is leaving Beiping tonight to go to Nanjing to wait to meet Huang Fu, as Huang Fu will be promoted to the capital soon to assume the position of Minister of the Interior concurrently. (Special Dispatch, 23rd)

The Completion of the Tombs of the Second Consorts of the Abdicated Qing Emperor

(Beiping) The coffins of the Second Consorts Yu and Jin of the abdicated Qing emperor were recently transported from Beiping to the Eastern Tombs for burial. Their tombs, constructed of cement, have now been fully completed, at a cost of over 20,000 yuan, far exceeding the amount required for previous consort burials. The Tongzhi Emperor's tomb was slightly damaged and was repaired at this time and is now completely restored. However, the Empress Dowager Cixi's tomb is in a state of disrepair. Qing Dynasty descendants began repairs during the fourth and fifth months of the lunar calendar. After the burial of the coffins of Consorts Yu and Jin, Zaiying went to Changchun to meet with the traitor Pu Yi to report on the progress and discuss the repair of the Empress Dowager Cixi's mausoleum. (23rd Dispatch)

Yu Fengzhi Seeks Medical Treatment at Peking Union Medical College

(Beiping) Yu Fengzhi is ill in Beiping and is seeking treatment at Peking Union Medical College. Madame Chiang Kai-shek, Soong Mei-ling, sent a telegram of condolence to Beiping. (23rd Dispatch)

Song Zheyuan Undergoes Physical Examination

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan went to Peking Union Medical College this morning for a physical examination. Song believes that his illness is cured and that the administration of the Chahar province urgently needs him to preside over it. He will return to Chahar with Qin Dechun, the director of the Chahar Civil Affairs Department, within the next few days. (23rd Dispatch)

International Commercial Telegraph

Special Reuters Commercial Dispatch of March 23

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Due to the rise in the value of the pound, the price of gold in London fell. Today's listing is 146 shillings and 1 penny, which is 4 and a half pence lower than yesterday.

London Silver Market: Today in London's silver market, due to good purchasing appetite from India and China and few sellers, the spot price is 27 and 375 pence and the futures price is 27 and a half pence, both higher by 1875 than yesterday. The market situation is quite stable.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market was quite tight today, with sluggish trading, but there is still an upward trend. The opening exchange rate for British-American was 4 yuan, 7 jiao, 6 fen, 875, which is 125 lower than yesterday's closing price for American-British. At 11:00, the price became slightly stronger due to trade winds, rising by 5625. Later, the buying subsided and the price fell back. However, the sentiment turned better at the close and the price was 4 yuan, 7 jiao, 125, which is 25 higher than the opening.

British-French: The opening price was 72 francs 31, which is 3 pounds lower than yesterday. There was some buying after the opening, so at 11:00 it rose by 4 pounds. There were no other characteristics. The closing price was 72 francs 34, which is 3 pounds higher than the opening.

American-British: The New York foreign exchange market was quite sluggish today. The opening price for British exchange was 4 yuan, 7 jiao, 7 fen, 25, which is 25 higher than yesterday's closing price. Later, it fell to 4 yuan, 7 jiao, 6 fen, 75.

American-French: The opening price for French exchange was 6 yuan, 5 jiao, 9 fen, 625, which is 25 lower than yesterday's closing price.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The opening price of the New York cotton market today was similar to yesterday's closing price. The market situation was more likely to fall, because of the brokers settling and foreign sales. Domestic counterparts bought in a little, anticipating that manufacturers will replenish some to offset sales before the price changes occur.

American Wheat: The price of the Chicago wheat market fell slightly today, but the market situation was stable after the price fell because the southwestern wheat area is still lacking rain. The opening price of Winnipeg wheat was stable and did not change in the first hour.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market rose with good sentiment in New York. Speculators and counterparts all bought in. At the close, the price for May was 6 pence 24, which is 13 pounds higher than yesterday's close.

British Wheat: The price of the Liverpool wheat market also rose today, because major wheat-producing countries all had bullish news. At the opening, the price for May was 5 shillings 3 pence 125, which is 25 higher than yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was slack. At noon, the trading price for July and September was 5 pence 4375, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: The New York rubber market opened down 10 pounds and did not improve afterward. There were few transactions and the market situation was slack.

Securities

New York: Inflation is now the main topic of conversation for Wall Street operators. After the bonus gold case was passed by the House of Representatives yesterday, talk of inflation is rampant again. However, although this case was passed by the House of Representatives by a large majority, those in charge do not hold much hope that it can be passed by the Senate, and the inevitable presidential veto must also be taken into account. President Roosevelt's opposition to the current form of the bonus gold case is well known, so if the inflationary nature of this case is not removed by the Senate, then this case may not become law. Before the opening of the securities market this morning, it was said that the market situation would definitely be affected by talk of inflation. However, although the market situation was slightly active at the opening, price fluctuations were still uneven. Public utility stocks were initially bought in, but as prices rose slightly, pressure followed. As a result, most stock prices still fell below yesterday's closing prices. Steel stocks opened up 25, at 30.25, but in less than 20 minutes, they fell to 29.75. Railway stocks did not change much. The New York securities market prices are listed on the left:

Train Derailment on the Jinpu Railway

(Jinan) Jinpu train No. 644 derailed at Huangheyai Station at 10 PM last night, blocking the line. Traffic was restored at 9:30 AM this morning. The Shanghai-Beiping northbound train was blocked at Zhangzhuang Station for 12 hours last night, and the southbound train was blocked at Dezhou for 9 hours. (23rd Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Beiping-Shanghai through train that should have arrived in Beiping this morning was unable to pass due to the derailment of a counterfeit freight car near Jinan on the 22nd. The Jinpu Railway Bureau urgently dispatched an engineering team to rescue it. After seven hours, traffic was restored. The Beiping-Shanghai train arrived in Beiping at 6:20 PM tonight, a total delay of seven and a half hours. (23rd Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Jinpu passenger train No. 302 was delayed for 7 hours at Dezhou due to the derailment of a coal train. It arrived in Tianjin at 2:10 PM on the 23rd. (23rd Dispatch)

The Embankment Project for the Luanhe Railway Bridge Has Been Completed

(Tianjin) All construction materials required for the reconstruction of the Luanhe Railway Bridge have been transported to Zhugezhuang. The embankment construction for the preparatory project has been completed. According to the person in charge of the Beining Railway Bureau's Engineering Department, the riverbed is currently being explored. The formal project is divided into two parts, the bridge body and the bridge foundation. If there are no obstacles due to weather or personnel, it can all be completed in three years. (23rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Xingsa Arrives in Jinan on His Way to Beiping

(Jinan) The Qinghai Living Buddha Xingsa Bandida passed through Jinan from Beijing today on his way to Beiping. He said he would stay in Beiping for a while and then return to Qinghai to prepare to welcome the Panchen Lama. The Panchen Lama is currently in Alashan, Xinjiang, and will definitely return to Tibet this year. Xingsa is scheduled to hold an enthronement ceremony in Qinghai next month and will return to Beijing next year. (23rd Dispatch)

Regulations for the Shandong Gold Mining Bureau Are Drafted

(Jinan) The regulations for the Gold Mining Bureau have been drafted and passed by the Provincial Government's Political Affairs Council. The bureau will be organized and attached to the Department of Construction. It will first mine the Hongshiqiao mineral deposits in Yishui, using self-made wooden boxes to mine gold, employing approximately 1,000 workers. (23rd Dispatch)

Yu Xuezhong Goes to Qingdao

(Jinan) Yu Xuezhong went to Qingdao tonight. Yu said that everything in Shandong is on track and better than other provinces. He will stay in Qingdao for three days and then return to his ancestral home in Penglai to sweep the tombs before returning to Tianjin. The provincial government will immediately move to Bao, and a garrison commander will be left in Tianjin to repair the Tianjin-Bao highway. (23rd Dispatch)

Han Fuju Summons Party Members in Stages for Instructions

(Jinan) Han Fuju said that starting on the 27th, he will summon lower-level party members from all over the province to Jinan in three stages for instructions. (23rd Dispatch)

Staff Delegation Stationed in Shaanxi Leaves Taiyuan

(Taiyuan) The director of the staff delegation stationed in Shaanxi, Mao Kan, and more than 80 others left Taiyuan at 7:00 AM on the 23rd, taking more than ten cars to western Shanxi and northern Shaanxi. They will make brief inspections along the way and are expected to arrive in Suide around the 28th. (23rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Directors of Various Henan Departments Give Public Banquet for Mao Weishou

(Kaifeng) The directors of various Henan departments, Li Peiji, etc., as well as members Zhang Zhonglu, etc., and the director of the Security Department, Feng Jianfei, gave a public banquet for Mao Weishou at the Department of Construction on the 23rd. (23rd Dispatch)

Henan Commissioner Wang Cifu Enters Sichuan

(Luoyang) Commander Chiang Kai-shek has transferred commissioners from Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and other provinces with good performance to Sichuan to improve Sichuan's administration. Wang Cifu, the commissioner of the tenth district of Henan, has been ordered to set off. (23rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Gansu Province Exempts Land Tax for Local Clearing

(Lanzhou) The Gansu Provincial Government meeting on the 19th passed a resolution to exempt the land tax for local clearing in various counties and cities one year ago in order to alleviate the people's difficulties. (23rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Director of Gansu Construction Department Goes to Jiangxi and Guangdong for Inspection

Public Telegram

Telegram from Anqing: To the editors of the Shenbao, Upon reading your newspaper's article on the 23rd of this month, "Anhui Business Federation requests a halt to tax increases," please note that the collection of business tax, tooth tax, slaughter tax, and tobacco and alcohol license taxes in this province has always been determined by the Finance Department based on the ratio of assessment. Currently, in order to eliminate embezzlement, a general order has been issued to increase the assessment ratio by 20%. As for the tax rates, they are strictly in accordance with the regulations, and there has been no increase in tax rates. We hereby request that your newspaper make immediate corrections to conform to the facts. Seal of the Finance Department of Anhui Province.

Stagnation in the Anhui Tea Market; Tight Credit Situation in Shanghai Reduces Lending by Tea Warehouses; Tea Merchants View Business with Trepidation After Droughts and Banditry

Wuhu Correspondence: The tea market in southern Anhui, which takes in Huizhou prefecture, has had a bountiful year. Trade and exports may take in around 20 million yuan in cash, which is truly vital for the livelihood of the people of Huizhou. The new tea will soon be available. In past years, at this time, Shanghai warehouses would extend loans to the countryside, tea merchants would raise funds to establish firms, and the tea market would be active. However, this spring, the weather has been warm and tea buds have flourished everywhere, but the activities of tea merchants are far less than before. It is said that one reason is that the establishment of tea firms in Huizhou depends on the amount of loans extended by Shanghai tea warehouses. In recent years, the credit situation in Shanghai has been extremely tight. Banks and money shops have adopted a tight lending policy to tea warehouses. Therefore, tea warehouses have had to narrow the scope of lending to tea firms. Furthermore, Huizhou was previously occupied and disturbed by bandits, causing great harm. Many wealthy families and tea merchants have taken refuge elsewhere. Although the banditry has been completely eliminated, distant places seem to still have some misunderstandings about the situation in Huizhou, causing some concerns. Therefore, there are only a few Shanghai warehouse merchants who have come to Huizhou, no more than three or so. The amount of money they plan to lend is also less than three-fifths of what they lent in previous years. The majority of other warehouse merchants are still considering and watching. As a result, tea merchants are waiting quietly for the arrival of warehouse merchants, and the tea market has fallen into a state of stagnation. Although some tea merchants used to have substantial assets, they have been repeatedly hit by droughts and banditry, and their economies have been severely damaged. The people's strength has declined sharply. In addition, the tea industry has suffered losses in foreign trade over the years, making investment in tea firms even more of a cause for trepidation. According to those familiar with the tea situation in Shanghai, the total amount of loans planned by Shanghai warehouses this year is less than six-tenths of last year. Based on this calculation, it is feared that no more than a hundred tea firms will be established this year. Liu Zhenhua, the chairman of Anhui Province, believes that Huizhou has been greatly damaged by bandits. Relying solely on fundraising for relief is not only practically difficult, but also difficult to achieve universal effect. Therefore, he attaches great importance to the revival of the Huizhou tea market. After clearing out the bandits, he immediately placed advertisements in various newspapers, hoping to recall the displaced people of Huizhou and encourage them to return to their homes as soon as possible so as not to miss the tea farming season again. The recovery of the tea market is the only way for the people of Huizhou to help themselves. However, the 383rd Regiment of the 64th Division stationed in Huizhou was originally planned to be transferred back to Qimen for consolidation pending departure from Huizhou. Later, in response to the request of the Tea Industry Association, it was ordered to continue to be stationed in various parts of Huizhou to be responsible for protecting the tea market and to search for remnant bandits in the mountainous areas between Qimen and Dezhou. (22nd)

Songjiang: Red Cross Branch Requests Preservation of Nijiatan

Li Xiuzhe of the Chinese Red Cross Society Sijing Branch and Zhou Xuewen of the Songjiang Branch recently submitted a report to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, stating that Nijiatan, located south of Malu Bridge outside the West Gate of Songjiang County, was originally the burial place of martyrs who died during the late Ming Dynasty and the Taiping Rebellion. The local gentry, Jiang Shilin, and others submitted a report to the county government in October of the fourth year of the Republic of China to prohibit the sale of the land. In the fourteenth year of the Republic of China, the people of Songjiang felt grateful to the Western missionary, Bu Huilian, for his efforts in maintaining the local area during repeated wars and raised funds to build a pavilion on it as a memorial. Unexpectedly, some unscrupulous local bullies have sold the land for profit, and seventy or eighty workers are transporting bricks and soil away every day, destroying graves. (Recently, a group of local bullies have made destroying ancient tombs their only quick way to make money.) They have also dismantled and destroyed the Bu Huilian Memorial Pavilion. If this trend continues, conspiracies will breed. Therefore, they appealed to the government of Songjiang County to immediately and strictly stop this practice and thoroughly investigate the sale of the land in order to comfort the loyal souls and protect the historical sites.

The Sufu Automobile Company is investing in the construction of the Sumu Road. After the road is open to traffic for three months, then lay down cobblestones to strengthen it. It is scheduled to be open to traffic by late May. The Suzhou station is located at the southern end of the Jinghu Road station outside Pingmen. The Mudu station is located in the central market of Mudu Town in the approach line area. The station buildings on both sides are under construction. The company is scheduled to hold its fifth board meeting on the 24th of this month to discuss and decide on all the progress guidelines.

At about 11:00 AM the day before yesterday, six refugee boats from other provinces arrived in Dajishan, Kaiyuan Township, Fourth District. Seeing that the house of Zhu De Kui was tall and large, they knew that he was wealthy. They rushed ashore and broke into Zhu's house, pulled out weapons, and threatened him not to make a sound. City Party Headquarters Passes Regulations for Honoring the Huanghuagang Martyrs

Meeting held at the Youth Propaganda Corps on the morning of the 29th, with seven organizations and groups, including the Municipal Government, appointed to the presidium

——All sectors of the city will fly flags at half-mast and observe a holiday on that day——

The Guominshe reports: The 29th of this month is the anniversary of the martyrdom of the seventy-two martyrs of Huanghuagang. In order to commemorate the revolutionary spirit of these martyrs and to inspire future generations to admire them, the City Party Headquarters of this city, in accordance with the central government's memorial principles, formulated memorial regulations, submitted them to the Executive Committee for approval, and appointed seven organizations and groups, including the City Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government, to form the presidium and hold a memorial meeting at the Youth Propaganda Corps. On that day, all sectors of the city will fly flags at half-mast and observe a holiday. The memorial regulations are as follows: (1) Convene a memorial assembly for revolutionary martyrs from all walks of life in Shanghai; (2) The venue will be the Youth Propaganda Corps in Xiaoximen; (3) The date is March 29th at 9:00 AM; (4) The presidium of the assembly will be composed of the City Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, the Garrison Headquarters, the Municipal Farmers' Association, the General Labor Union, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the Municipal Education Association; (5) The investigation section comrades will be responsible for maintaining order at the assembly, and the publicity section comrades will be responsible for reception, announcements, and recording; (6) Starting from March 27th, publish a notice in the newspaper for three days to inform all sectors to take a holiday on that day and send representatives to participate; (7) Send a letter to the Municipal Education Bureau to instruct all schools in the city to send ten representatives to participate in the assembly; (8) Send a letter to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to dispatch some police officers to maintain order at the venue and send a military band to the venue to play music; (9) The publicity section will draft and distribute a "Letter to the Public Commemorating Revolutionary Martyrs."

Ministry of Finance Issues Financial Bonds to Increase Capital for Three Banks

Central and Communications Banks decide to submit proposal at the upcoming shareholders' meeting; Director of Public Debt arrives in Shanghai to discuss issuance methods

The Xinsheng News Agency reports: In order to rescue the market, the Ministry of Finance is issuing 100 million yuan of financial bonds for the 24th year of the Republic of China to supplement the capital of the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. These three banks have separately scheduled general shareholders' meetings and board meetings to submit and approve the proposal. Details are recorded as follows:

Director Jiang Arrives in Shanghai to Discuss Issuance

The 150 million yuan financial bonds for the 24th year of the Republic of China have been approved by the Central Political Conference and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. After the regulations are passed, they will be issued immediately. Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance, arrived in Shanghai from the capital the day before yesterday and immediately met with Minister Kong Xiangxi to request instructions on everything. At the same time, yesterday afternoon, he met with Zhang Gongquan, General Manager of the Bank of China, and Tang Shoumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, to discuss the issuance of financial bonds. It is heard that it has been decided to handle it according to past methods, so the issuance of these bonds is no longer a problem.

Total Capital of the Central Bank Increased

The total capital of the Central Bank is 20 million yuan in national currency, and the paid-in capital is 20 million yuan in national currency, allocated by the Ministry of Finance. Last year, the government decided to expand the capital of the bank to 100 million yuan, so this time another 30 million yuan of financial bonds for the 24th year of the Republic of China will be allocated to make up the difference. According to the regulations, "If it is necessary to increase capital due to business needs, the board of directors shall decide, the board of supervisors shall agree, and the matter shall be submitted to the National Government for approval to expand the total capital, and commercial shares may be solicited, but commercial shares shall not exceed 49% of the total capital." Now the bank will submit the matter to the board of directors and the board of supervisors for approval.

History of the Capital of the Central and Communications Banks

(1) Bank of China (International Exchange Bank): The total capital is 25 million yuan in national currency, and the paid-in capital is 24,712,200 yuan in national currency. The number of shares is 250,000, each share being 100 yuan. The government owns 50,000 shares, that is, 5 million yuan, and commercial shares are 200,000 shares, that is, 20 million yuan. This time, 25 million yuan of financial bonds for the 24th year of the Republic of China will be allocated to increase capital, bringing the total to 50 million yuan. (2) Bank of Communications (National Industrial Development Bank): The total capital is 10 million yuan in national currency, and the paid-in capital is 8,715,600 yuan in national currency. The number of shares is 100,000, each share being 100 yuan. The government owns 20,000 shares, that is, 2 million yuan, and commercial shares are 80,000 shares, that is, 8 million yuan. This time, 10 million yuan of financial bonds for the 24th year of the Republic of China will be allocated to increase capital, bringing the total to 20 million yuan.

Regulations Stipulate Shareholder Approval

Article 2 of the regulations of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications stipulates that "If it is necessary to increase capital stock due to business needs, the matter may be decided by the general shareholders' meeting and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval." A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency specifically inquired with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications yesterday and learned that the regular general shareholders' meetings of the two banks have been scheduled to be held in Shanghai, and all shareholders have been notified. The proposal to allocate the capital of the two banks with the financial bonds issued by the Ministry of Finance in the 24th year of the Republic of China will be submitted to the regular general shareholders' meeting for approval and then submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval in accordance with the regulations.

General Shareholders' Meetings to Be Held Separately

(1) Bank of China Notice: The board of directors of this bank has decided that the 18th regular general shareholders' meeting of this year will be held at 1:00 PM on March 30th in the meeting hall of the Banking Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road, Shanghai. Shareholders who meet the membership qualifications stipulated in Article 40 of the bank's articles of association (shareholders who have been registered for more than ten shares for 60 days or more counting from the date of the meeting) are requested to bring their new shares, old shares, or application forms for changing shares to the head office or branches of this bank before the meeting to verify and obtain admission slips. And it is hoped that from five days before the meeting to the day before the meeting, the admission slip will be used to exchange for admission tickets at the head office for attending the meeting. If you are unable to attend due to an accident, you can submit a power of attorney after verifying the admission slip and hand it over to a shareholder attending the meeting as an agent. Furthermore, the exchange of new shares will be temporarily suspended for 30 days before the meeting and will continue after the meeting. In addition to sending letters, this is a special announcement. (2) Bank of Communications Notice: Dear shareholders of the Bank of Communications, this bank has decided that the regular general shareholders' meeting of this year will be held at 1:00 PM on April 20th (Gregorian calendar) at the Banking Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road. All shareholders are requested to bring their shares to the head office on the Bund of Sanma Road in Shanghai from ten days before the meeting to two days before the meeting to verify and obtain admission tickets, or go to the nearest branch to verify the attendance certificate with the shares and bring it to the head office to exchange for admission tickets on the aforementioned date. Those who are unable to attend in person and need to entrust a representative should be limited to members in accordance with Articles 16 and 17 of the bank's regulations, and please bring the shares in person to the nearest branch in advance to list the account name and number of shares, fill in the power of attorney, and have the branch verify and stamp it, and hand it over to the representative to bring it to the head office for verification and collection of admission tickets so that they can attend the meeting at that time. In addition to sending separate letters, this is a special announcement.

Decision to pay in three installments, with 500,000 yuan paid by the end of the month; Changsha branches of the three banks will directly deliver to the Hunan Provincial Government

Shanghai Municipal Council Approves Telephone Price Increase After Discussion; Maximum Increase of 12.5% Requires Consent of the French Concession; Other Matters Concerning Management Fees to Be Discussed Separately

The Shanghai Telephone Company petitioned the Municipal Council to revise the tariff rates starting from April of this year. The Municipal Council has now allowed the company to increase its total revenue by a maximum of 12.5%. The company must separately draft new tariff regulations, carefully allocate them, and then wait for review and decision. It is also reported that the company has recently claimed that the number of telephones has decreased by about 1,000 in the past two and a half months, while the previous estimate was that it could increase by 800. Therefore, due to the difference between the two, future income will be far less than expected. The contents of the company's petition and the discussion of the Public Utilities Committee of the Municipal Council are recorded separately as follows:

Assets and Liabilities

According to the company's report, as of 1934, the investment items included capital stock of 8,052,000 yuan (all calculated in Chinese national currency, omitting thousands), company bonds of 24,675,000 yuan, and loans with a term of more than one year of 2,098,000 yuan, totaling 34,825,000 yuan. The company's income, including telephone charges and other income for that year, was 6,625,000 yuan. The expenditure items included telephone service fees of 1,025,000 yuan, maintenance fees of 875,000 yuan, business expenses of 695,000 yuan, depreciation of 1,597,000 yuan, and donations and taxes of 140,000 yuan, totaling 4,332,000 yuan. After deducting interest and other payments of more than 130,000 yuan, the net profit was 2,159,000 yuan, equivalent to about 6.13% of the investment.

New Tariff Method

According to the company's franchise contract, the company should have a net profit annual interest rate of 1% (i.e., 8%) plus a reserve fund of 2% starting from April last year. Therefore, according to the company's calculation, based on the figures for 1934, there is still a shortage of about 1,362,000 yuan in income. In order to make up for this shortage, the company intends to increase the current telephone charges by an average of 23% (22.89%). For this purpose, the company proposes to revise the tariff method, the most important of which is to change all commercial telephones to a per-call charging method.

Commercial Telephones

The current commercial telephones have two types of charges: one is fixed, at 12.24 yuan per line per month, and the other is limited to 300 calls for 12.24 yuan, 500 calls for 13.8 yuan, 700 calls for 15.69 yuan, and an additional charge of 0.0559 yuan per call for more than 700 calls. The company intends to uniformly change to a per-call charge, with 10 yuan per month for 100 calls or less, an additional charge of 0.05 yuan per call for 100 to 200 calls, an additional charge of 0.04 yuan per call for 200 to 300 calls, and an additional charge of 0.03 yuan per call for more than 300 calls.

Residential Telephones

The current telephone charge for residential telephones is 7.58 yuan per month, and the company intends to increase it to 8.5 yuan. In addition, the fees for private lines, extension lines, and branch lines, and branch line exchanges will all be increased, while the fees for switching and reconnecting will be reduced. The installation and relocation fees, which were previously uniformly 13.99 yuan, will be changed to 15 yuan for commercial use and 10 yuan for home use in the future. The total result of various increases and decreases is estimated to increase total revenue by about 22.89%. According to this method, the company can obtain an average net profit of 10.08% per year from April 1 of this year to April 1, 1937.

Discussion Process

The company's request to increase prices has been discussed in detail by the Public Utilities Committee of the Municipal Council. At the same time, the Foreign Exchange Brokers Association, the Japanese Residents Group, and the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce have all sent letters to the Municipal Council expressing their objections. The basis for the company's calculation of profits and losses, such as the issue of income tax payable to the United States, the issue of depreciation reserve funds, and the management fees paid to the International Telephone and Telegraph Company, all need to be studied. And the company's prediction that the number of calls will be reduced by half after charging by the number of calls seems to be too optimistic. According to the opinion of the Director of Finance, the income tax item (according to the company's calculation, 850,000 yuan will be needed in the next two years) is not within the scope of the contract and should not be borne by the users. Regarding the depreciation item, the Municipal Council assisted the company with a loan at the end of the previous year to convert its foreign currency debts into silver currency debts. Therefore, the investment should be reduced by 3 million yuan, and the annual depreciation amount can also be greatly reduced as a result. As for the management fees paid to the International Company, which are calculated at 4.5% of the total income per year, requiring about 300,000 yuan, this matter should not be a burden for Shanghai for a long time. Therefore, according to the opinion of the Director of Finance, if the company's income can increase by 12.5% per year, it will be enough for the company to obtain a net profit of 1%. As for the distribution items of the price increase, it should be further considered. According to the company's opinion, if the shareholders cannot obtain a considerable interest, it will be difficult to raise capital again in the future. However, the Director of Finance said that if the 12.5% ​​quota is collected, the shareholders can actually obtain a dividend of about 1.5%, and future expansion will no longer require huge sums of money, and it may be possible to raise funds locally. However, from the perspective of the Municipal Council, other public utilities can all pay dividends on time, so it seems impossible not to allow the telephone company to obtain a considerable profit. Moreover, in the past fifteen months, the company's operating expenses have been saved by about 400,000 yuan per year, and there is no problem with its engineering efficiency. Furthermore, according to the company's calculation two years ago, the price increase needs to be more than 40% in order to reach the conditions permitted by the contract. After using various methods to deal with it, the current increase is only 12.5%, which can be said to have reasonable protection for the interests of users.

Permission to Increase

After careful consideration, the Public Utilities Committee decided to recommend to the board of directors that the company be allowed to increase its income by a maximum of 12.5% ​​starting from April 1 of this year, but it must also obtain the consent of the French Concession authorities, and the allocation method of the price increase must also be permitted by the two concessions. As for other issues such as income tax, depreciation, and management fees, they will be discussed separately.

Two US Inspection Delegations Scheduled to Arrive in China One After Another; Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce Inspection Delegation to Arrive in Shanghai Tomorrow; US Economic Inspection Delegation to Arrive on the 22nd of Next Month

The Xinxin News Agency reports: The Far East Commercial Inspection Delegation organized by the Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce of the United States, consisting of more than 20 people, has arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong on the President Hoover. It is expected to arrive at the port on the afternoon of the 25th. As for the Far East Economic Inspection Delegation organized by the American International Association, it is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the 22nd of next month. All sectors of the city have prepared to welcome them. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce Inspection Delegation

The Far East Commercial Inspection Delegation organized by the Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce of the United States, consisting of more than 20 people, arrived in Hong Kong from the Philippines on the 22nd and took the Dollar Steamship Company's President Hoover to Shanghai on the 22nd. According to the company's news, the President Hoover is scheduled to arrive at the port at 4:30 PM on the 25th and dock at the Bailianjing Pier in Pudong. According to the Xinxin News Agency reporter, the members of the delegation are all well-known American businessmen. Their task is to investigate the commercial situation of the United States in China. Therefore, after the delegation arrives in Shanghai, it will go to Hangzhou and then to North China for investigation. After staying in China for about three weeks, it plans to go to Kobe and return to the country.

US Far East Economic Inspection Delegation

The American Far East Business Economic Inspection Delegation organized by the American International Association, consisting of 16 members, is composed of well-known figures from various sectors such as finance, industry, and transportation in the United States. A reporter from the Xinxin News Agency went to the China International Trade Association yesterday morning to inquire about the delegation's arrival in China. According to the association, the delegation has already departed from San Francisco for China on the 22nd and will arrive in Yokohama, Japan on April 5th. It will arrive in Shanghai on April 22nd. After the delegation arrives in Shanghai, it plans to divide into teams to investigate the actual situation in the interior, and then return to Shanghai to discuss the development of Sino-US trade issues with various sectors at home and abroad before returning to the country on schedule.

The Two Delegations Have Different Missions in China

Although the names of the two inspection delegations are similar, they have different purposes. The Far East Commercial Inspection Delegation organized by the Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce of the United States aims only to understand the recent commercial situation of the United States in China so that it can have a better understanding of Sino-US trade in the future. It is entirely a commercial organization. As for the Far East Economic Inspection Delegation organized by the American International Trade Association, its mission is more important. The purpose of the delegation is to collect various materials needed for Sino-US trade, as well as the situation of American investment in China, and to study methods for developing Sino-US trade with our country. Therefore, its mission has an important meaning for the entire future of Sino-US trade.

Various Circles in China and the United States Prepare to Welcome Them

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the National Committee of the International Chamber of Commerce, the China International Trade Association, and other organizations believe that the American Far East Business Economic Inspection Delegation's visit to China for investigation will be of considerable benefit to Sino-US trade. They have initiated a welcome rally, and various organizations have discussed the welcome arrangements several times. It has now been decided to organize a reception office for the American Far East Commercial Inspection Delegation to take charge of everything. The office is actively preparing and will be formally established soon to start work. As for foreign companies, such as the British-American Tobacco Company, the Dollar Steamship Company, and the Shanghai Power Company, they are also making contacts and preparing to welcome them separately. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Steamships: Adoption of the New Metric Ton System

Notice to All Merchants and Crew Members: To be Implemented Starting April 1st

Changing to the New Metric Ton

The adoption of the metric ton system for ships has been agreed upon by the Jianghai Customs and the Ministry of Transportation, and will be implemented starting the first day of the [lunar] month. There are a total of six principles. The local [Shanghai] Maritime Bureau has already notified all merchants and crew members, stating briefly, "We have received Circular No. 49 from the Navigation Administration Bureau, which forwards Instruction No. 652 from the Ministry of Transportation. All ships should adopt the metric ton system in accordance with the Maritime Law. The Ministry of Industry has instructed the National Bureau of Weights and Measures to draft six principles, which should be implemented on a trial basis. It is hereby decided to implement them starting April 1st. The various principles, with annotations, are now issued for all crew members to follow." Attached is a copy of the six principles for the uniformity of navigation administration weights and measures as follows:

Six Principles

(1) The measurement of ships is limited to the use of meters, but private ships may use Chinese feet [市尺], provided that the equivalent in meters is also indicated. (Note: This Bureau is a state-run organization and should use meters as the standard. One meter is equivalent to 3.28 British/American feet, one British/American foot is equivalent to 0.3048 meters, and one meter is equivalent to three Chinese feet.) (2) The measurement of ship volume should follow the precedents of countries that have adopted the metric system, stipulating that 2.83 cubic meters is one ton, known as a volume ton. To calculate the volume tonnage of a ship, measure the length, width, and height of the ship in meters, multiply them together to obtain the cubic meters, and then divide by 2.83 to obtain the tonnage. Article 15 of Chapter 4 of the Ship Measurement Regulations, "Tonnage Calculation," is to be amended to read, "The volume of a ship is calculated with 2.83 cubic meters (equivalent to 100 cubic feet) as one volume ton. For ships whose capacity is expressed in piculs [擔], 0.283 cubic meters (equivalent to 10 cubic feet) is considered a 'volume picul.'" (Note: Ship volume tons are used to calculate the gross and net tonnage. Using 2.83 cubic meters as one volume ton is, in effect, equivalent to 100 cubic feet. However, the measurement should be based on the metric system. This section relates to the payment of tonnage dues to the Navigation Administration Bureau and this Bureau, and is usually not relevant to the duties of senior crew members.) (3) For goods transported by ships that are valued by weight, standard weight names should be used, such as metric tons, metric piculs, etc., or Chinese weight names, such as Chinese piculs, Chinese catties [斤], etc. For goods valued by volume, the space they occupy should be measured in cubic meters (equivalent to the number of cubic Chinese feet) or cubic Chinese feet (equivalent to the number of cubic meters). If necessary, 1.13 cubic meters may be used as a cargo volume ton. (Note: The cargo tonnage calculated by weight is what the English call "Dead-Weight Ton." The current standard of one metric ton is one thousand kilograms, equivalent to 2204.62 pounds in the English system. The cargo ton calculated by volume is what the English call "Measurement Ton." Using 1.13 cubic meters as a cargo volume ton is, in effect, equivalent to 40 cubic feet. However, the measurement should be based on the metric system.) (4) The distance used to calculate the price of a ship should be in kilometers or Chinese li [市里]. (Note: One kilometer is one thousand meters, equivalent to two Chinese li, or 0.62137 miles. This unit is different from nautical miles and is only used for calculating the price of a ship. It is not related to navigation. See item 5 below for how nautical miles are defined.) (5) The nautical mile used for ocean navigation should be 1852 meters, in accordance with international regulations (equivalent to 1.852 kilometers) (i.e., divide the Earth's meridian line, which is 360 degrees, into 60 minutes per degree, and take the distance of one minute as one nautical mile). (Note: The nautical mile still uses the distance of one minute of the Earth's meridian line as the standard, and there is no actual change from the English/American system of 6080 feet per nautical mile.) (6) The specification for ship pressure, originally using "pounds per square inch," should be changed to "kilograms per square centimeter," but the number of pounds may be noted for transitional purposes. (Note: "One pound per square inch" is equivalent to 0.07031 "kilograms per square centimeter" or 0.06804 "atmospheres." One "kilogram per square centimeter" is equivalent to 14.223 "pounds per square inch" or 0.9678 "atmospheres." One "atmosphere" is equivalent to 14.70 "pounds per square inch" or 1.0333 "kilograms per square centimeter.") If crew members still have any unclear points regarding the above principles and notes, they may inquire at the department at any time.

Three Beihai-Shanghai Steamer "Hongzhen" Aground and Rescued

Stranded at Zhishan below Yichang; "Yian" Steamer Tows and Rescues to Shanghai

The Three Beihai Company's Shanghai-bound steamer "Hongzhen" ran aground this Wednesday while traveling downstream from Yichang to Shanghai. The ship was fully loaded with cargo. It had first arrived in Hankou and was originally scheduled to depart from Hankou on the 22nd to return to Shanghai. However, after the ship departed from Yichang, it encountered fog and the river level dropped. Due to the negligence of the river pilot, the "Hongzhen" ran aground in the Zhishan area of the river, downstream from Yichang and upstream from Hankou. At the time, the ship was heavily laden with cargo and had a deep draft, causing it to become stuck in the shallows and impossible to free on its own. The owner of the "Hongzhen" immediately telegraphed the Yichang branch office to report the incident and request assistance. The Yichang branch office, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched the "Yian" steamer to the Zhishan river area to attempt to lighten the "Hongzhen" by offloading some of its cargo, and then to tow it free. Yesterday, this newspaper received a telegram stating that the "Hongzhen" had been towed free from the shallows by the "Yian" steamer and was now proceeding back to Shanghai. Whether the ship sustained any damage will be determined after it arrives in Shanghai and the cargo is unloaded.

Xu Shiying Returns to Shanghai Yesterday; Discusses Spring Relief Loans

Government and Local Authorities to Each Bear Half; $200,000 Interest-Free Loans to Farmers

According to the Guowen News Agency, Mr. Xu Jingren (Xu Shiying), Chairman of the National Relief Commission and Vice Chairman of the Famine Relief Association of Various Provinces, has returned to Shanghai by train at 11:35 p.m. the night before after reporting on the past year's relief efforts to the central government and seeking instructions on spring relief matters. Yesterday, he spoke to reporters from the Guowen News Agency, saying that regarding the interest-free loans for spring seeds, he had repeatedly consulted with President Wang, Minister Kong, and Mr. Ye Chucang, and decided that the government would allocate $200,000 for the purchase of seeds to be distributed to farmers in various disaster-stricken provinces. The provincial governments of each province will bear half of the cost. For example, Jiangsu Province will receive $20,000 from the National Relief Commission, plus $20,000 from the provincial government, for a total of $40,000 to purchase seeds to loan to farmers without interest, to be repaid after the autumn harvest. The number of funds allocated to each province and the method of lending will be determined at a regular meeting of the Standing Committee at Renji Hall at 4:00 p.m. on the 27th of this month (next Wednesday). The funds will generally be advanced by the Central Bank. As for the $600,000 in famine relief funds allocated by the central government to the provinces, $550,000 has already been received. Of the remaining $50,000, $5,000 has been directly allocated by the Ministry of Finance to the Nanjing Municipal Government, and the remaining $45,000 was to be collected from the Central Bank today (yesterday) and dispatched to the designated provinces. The winter emergency relief effort last year has now concluded. In addition, construction work on Huangshan Mountain has begun this year. More than 90 households have registered to claim state-owned land, and about 30 have reported. Fundraising efforts are underway to complete the original plan. He (Xu himself) is scheduled to go to Hangzhou on the 18th and then to Huangshan Mountain for inspection.

Real Estate Developer Discusses Circulating Notes; Proposes Reducing Issuance by 300 Million Yuan

Yesterday, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency interviewed a real estate developer about the issue of issuing real estate circulating notes. According to the developer, the proposed issuance of circulating notes has been under consideration for a long time and has been discussed with the government beforehand. Since the total value of Shanghai real estate is 1.8 billion yuan, and assuming that 800 million yuan is held by foreign merchants, then the real estate owned by Chinese merchants is worth 1 billion yuan. Therefore, it would not be excessive to issue 500 million yuan in circulating notes, which is half the value. Even if some of the 1 billion yuan in real estate cannot be circulated due to other reasons, assuming that the amount of non-circulating assets is 400 million yuan, there would still be 600 million yuan in assets that could be circulated. Even if that 600 million yuan were calculated at half the value, 300 million yuan in circulating notes could still be issued. Furthermore, all of the real estate developers' deeds would be stored in the national treasury at the time of issuance. If a real estate developer were to experience personal issues, the government could confiscate all of their assets to compensate for the loss. Even if real estate were to gradually decline in value in the future, it would certainly not fall below half the value. Therefore, the issuance of circulating notes backed by real estate is more reliable than other empty guarantees. At a minimum, the real estate developers must insist on issuing 300 million yuan in circulating notes.

On the Steamer "Xin Renhe", A Young Couple Commits Suicide by Jumping into the River; Despairing of the World Due to Marital Problems; The Owner Stopped the Ship to Rescue but it was Too Late

The steamer "Xin Renhe," which travels between Chongming, Haimen, Qidong, and Shanghai, departed from Wharf No. 5 in southern Shanghai at 5:00 p.m. on the 21st of this month, bound for the ports of Haimen and Qidong. At 7:45 p.m., while passing the waters near the floating dock west of the Lion Mountain outside Wusongkou, passengers reported that a young man and woman simultaneously jumped into the river from the stern of the second-class deck and committed suicide. The owner immediately stopped the ship and turned around to attempt a rescue, which took 45 minutes. At that time, the tide was ebbing, the northeast wind was strong, and the current was swift, making rescue impossible. At the time, the steward Huang Can reported that around 4:00 p.m. that day, a young man and woman came aboard and booked cabin No. 4 on the third-class deck. When the ship passed Wusongkou, they ordered fried rice with eggs, boiled chicken, shrimp and pickled vegetable soup, and white wine from the steward. After the kitchen had prepared the food and brought it up, the two were nowhere to be found. While everyone was wondering what happened, they suddenly heard that a man and a woman had jumped into the river. The owner, together with the compradore and other crew members, inspected the cabin and found a suicide note written in pencil on a piece of antique copper paper on the table. They also found a handbag containing powder, some paper money and copper coins, and other items. It became clear that the young man and woman who jumped into the river from the stern of the second-class deck were the same two people who had booked cabin No. 4 on the third-class deck. Upon reading the contents of the suicide note, it was learned that the man's name was Gong Wu'gao (signed "Shi Shang"), from Huilong Town, Qidong, and the woman's name was Zhang Xueqing, from Ningbo. The reason for their suicide seemed to be marital problems. In addition to instructing Yang Xiqing, the director of the Antougang branch office, to notify their families, the remaining items and suicide notes were reported to the Navigation Administration Bureau for record-keeping. The suicide note is as follows:

Two Respectful Letters

Before Dear Parents: I humbly report that my unfilial crime is as heavy as the sky. I will repay your kindness of raising me in the next life. You both love your son as if he were a pearl in your palm. My suicide today is due to the coercion of my mother and elder sister, and the harshness of the environment. I hope you will not be sad, but think of me as having died from a sudden illness, or an early death in childhood. I have now seen through the ways of the world, and everything is an illusion, so I do not wish to live in this bustling world. I and Miss Xueqing are bound together by love and cannot be separated, so we are boarding a ship to seek death. We will live together in life, and die together in death. My words are not finished, but the end has come. I will say no more, but speak to you in my dreams. Your son Gong Shi Shang, your daughter-in-law Zhang Xueqing, prostrate themselves. (2) Before Dear Grandmother: I humbly report that since leaving Qidong for Chongming, I have suffered greatly. The other day, my mother colluded with my maternal grandmother to file a lawsuit, reported me to the public security authorities, and I was deported. I had no face to return home and did not want to live anymore. My suicide today is for no other reason than that I have seen through the ways of the world, so I do not wish to live in this world. Your grandson and granddaughter-in-law have now jumped into the sea together. Please do not be sad. I wish you all the best. Your grandson Gong Shi Shang, your granddaughter-in-law Zhang Xueqing, prostrate themselves.

Letter to the Reporter: Dear Reporter, I want to trouble you. Please publish the following paragraph in the newspaper: "The reason for our death, due to our inseparable love, is entirely due to the coercion of our mother and elder sister in the family. They wanted to force us apart, and we could not bear to separate, so we came to Shanghai to jump into the river." Today, we drank our farewell wine at the Great China Restaurant, and then watched a play at the Golden Theater. The woman is from Ningbo, 25 years old, named Zhang Xueqing. The man is from Qidong, 20 years old, named Gong Minggao. I also hope that the following poems will be published. Written jointly by the man and woman:

Three Farewell Poems

(1) Leaving the world to say goodbye to Shanghai, only for you, abandoning my white hair and burdening you again. We have enjoyed sorrow and joy together in life, and we will sink together in the vast sea. (2) Holding a pen, I write a poem with great enthusiasm, the words in the poem are extraordinary. I regret that my Xiao Xiang [a river in Hunan] has no shadows of flowers, and is also in the spring flowing in the drizzle. (3) I was born in Tangjia Village, Si Jing [near Shanghai], my father is in prison in Chongcheng. The woman lives with her mother, enjoying freedom in the countryside.

A Rogue, Utterly Desperate and Bored, Impersonates a Landlord to Defraud

Using Someone Else's House as His Own; Claims to Reduce Rent to Deceive and Obtain Rental Income

There are two houses with old addresses No. 18 and No. 20, at Rue Ratard and Rue Albert, French Concession, now renumbered by the Municipal Council as No. 56 and No. 58. They are the property of Hongyu Real Estate Company. They were previously rented to Hengxingxiang Foreign Goods Store. Recently, due to poor market conditions, the store went bankrupt and returned the property, which has been vacant. A "For Rent" notice has been posted on the door. However, a rogue named Wang Wentai (33 years old, from Wuxi, residing at No. 3, Ronghua Lane, Old West Gate), desperate and bored, had the outlandish idea of posing as the owner of the house and spreading the word that he was reducing the rent to attract renters. Liu Jinkang, a Suzhou native who runs a butcher shop at No. 393, Gonghe Road, Zhabei, was planning to find a house to open a business and heard this news. He contacted Wang on the 6th of this month to rent the two houses, agreeing on a monthly rent of 147 yuan, including small repairs. He paid a deposit of 10 yuan and agreed to sign a lease. However, Wang could not wait and sent a letter urging Liu to pay the rent quickly, otherwise someone else would rent the house before him. After receiving the letter, Liu paid Wang 200 yuan in rent on the 10th of the same month. Wang issued a receipt from the "Hengji Company Rental Office" for the fourth month of the 24th year [of the Republic, 1935] to Liu as proof of renting the house. Liu immediately hired workers to renovate the storefront on the following day. On the 13th, Hongyu Real Estate Company, the real owner of the house, found out and stopped Liu from renovating. Only then did Liu realize that he had been deceived. He sought out Wang Wentai to argue and demand the return of his money, but Wang had already disappeared. Liu reported the incident to the French police and requested an investigation. It turns out that after Wang Wentai received the money from Liu, he used the same method to rent the two houses to three Suzhou natives living at No. 6, Ren Zhi Lane, Mofang Street: Gao Quansheng, Xu Yunqing, and Xia Keming, to open a game meat store. They had agreed on a monthly rent of 125 yuan, a tip of 100 yuan, and an opening fee of 10 yuan. They were scheduled to pay the rent and tip at the Qunleju teahouse at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Zhengjia Bridge Street at 10:00 a.m. the day before (the 21st) to sign a lease. While the two sides were negotiating, Liu Jinkang, who had been previously deceived, found out and reported it to the Mailand Station police. Detective Li Baochang accompanied Liu to the Qunleju teahouse, arrested Wang Wentai, and brought him and Gao, Xu, and Xia to the police station. After questioning by the police chief, Gao, Xu, and Xia also told the police that Wang had attempted to defraud them and requested an investigation. The police chief ordered Wang to be detained and sent to the Second Special District Court yesterday. Judge Qiu Huan-ying presided over the Eighth Criminal Court for the trial. Police lawyer Yuan Jiahong stated the case, saying that the defendant was arrested for fraudulently obtaining property and requested a postponement so that the police could thoroughly investigate the case before formally prosecuting. Liu Jinkang, the plaintiff, then recounted his experience of being deceived and said that Jiang Afu was present and witnessed the payment. When questioning the defendant Wang Wentai, Wang denied that he was employed by Hongyu Real Estate Company and denied deceiving Liu, claiming that he had been falsely accused. The court adjourned the hearing to the 26th and ordered the defendant to be remanded and the plaintiff to bring his witness to court for questioning at the next hearing.

Kidnappers Are Outrageously Rude and Scold the Judge; Retrial of the Kidnapping of Wei Tingrong; Kidnapper Zhu Jingcheng Shouts That He Would Rather Be Shot

Wei Tingrong, the former commander of the French Concession Chinese Volunteer Corps, director of the French Municipal Council's Chinese Affairs Committee, manager of the Sino-French Bank, and a native of Ningbo, was kidnapped on Zhubao Road at noon on July 24, 1929. After the French police rescued him, they arrested the gang members Zhu Jincheng, i.e., Zhu Jingcheng (also known as Xiangfeng, 37 years old, from Huaining, Anhui, formerly employed by the Anhui Department of Finance and the Jiangsu Water Police Department), Chen Zhongheng (also known as Chen Wangkui, 35 years old, from Wenzhou, Zhejiang), and Tang Shiliang (36 years old, from Songjiang). The French police sent them to the former French Concession Court, which sentenced them to five years of imprisonment each, to be handed over to the mainland government for trial after serving their sentences. Now that the five-year sentences of Zhu and the other two have expired, and because the French Concession Court has been taken back and the Chinese courts and prisons have been established, the Second Special District Prison has transferred Zhu and the other two to the Second Special District Court to be reviewed. Judge Qiu Huan-ying has held two hearings and has also transferred the files of the gang members Lü Ruowang and Li Weicai, who have already been sentenced to life imprisonment, for verification. Zhu and the others have denied being involved in the kidnapping and have hired lawyers to defend themselves. The debate has concluded, and a date has been set for sentencing. This has been previously reported. Yesterday was the date of sentencing. Judge Qiu presided over the Eighth Criminal Court and ordered the three defendants to be brought before the court. After briefly questioning their names and birthplaces, he announced the verdict: Zhu Jincheng, for instigating kidnapping for ransom, is sentenced to seven years of imprisonment. Chen Zhongheng and Tang Shiliang, for assisting in kidnapping for ransom, are each sentenced to six years of imprisonment. The number of days they have been in prison will be counted as time served. After the verdict, the judge briefly explained the reasons for the verdict to Zhu and the others. Zhu showed an arrogant attitude and asked the court, "How much time do I have left? Has the one-third reduction in sentence been deducted? My case is really unfair. Please (referring to the judge) have mercy." The judge said that kidnapping should originally be punishable by death, and that reducing the sentence to seven years of imprisonment was already very lenient. If he was not satisfied, he could appeal to the High Third Branch Court after receiving the judgment. At this point, Zhu glared and shouted, "I am not satisfied! I would rather be shot!" and cursed the judge for an unfair verdict. The court, hearing this, was greatly angered and ordered the bailiffs to take him down to be sent to the prosecutor's office for investigation and prosecution. As Zhu was being taken down by the police, he continued to curse. However, Chen and Tang remained silent and showed a pitiful state of fear.

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Announcement; Prohibiting the Reception of Gods and Religious Processions

Wasting Money and Harming Public Order; Vigorously Promoting the New Life Movement and Eliminating Superstition

Cai Jingjun, the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, issued a special order to all branch bureaus and police stations yesterday to comply with the prohibition of the evil practice of receiving gods and religious processions, and issued a notice stating, "The reception of gods and religious processions disrupts the law and order, and has been repeatedly prohibited by announcements. According to reports, there have been incidents of raising gods and holding processions in Yangjing Town and Tangqiao during the Qingming Festival this year, which is completely inappropriate. It must be understood that such actions not only waste money and manpower, but also create opportunities for local ruffians to extort money and cause trouble, which greatly harms public order. At a time when the New Life Movement is being vigorously promoted, there should be no promotion of such superstitious practices. The ban should be reiterated to maintain public order. In addition to ordering subordinates to strictly prohibit it, this announcement is hereby made for general information. All must comply and must not deliberately violate it."

Dancer's Abortion Case; Midwife Found Guilty and Sentenced

Sentenced to One Year and Six Months of Imprisonment, Suspended for Three Years; Chen Weida Proves No Involvement with Documents

Bao Huiying, a dancer at the La Dahua Dance Hall, became pregnant recently as a result of a physical relationship with a customer. The pregnancy had reached three months, and her abdomen was gradually expanding. As she made her living by dancing, a large abdomen would be unsightly and would greatly affect her work. She learned that Liu Wangshi, a midwife residing at No. 723, Jiujiang Road, was accustomed to performing abortions. On the 4th of this month, she went to Liu Wangshi's place and begged her to perform an abortion. Although the fetus was aborted, the dancer's internal organs were damaged. Her father, Bao Zhenyuan, sent her to Guangren Hospital for treatment at 4:00 p.m. on the 11th, but she died of her injuries at 6:00 p.m. that night. After the incident, the local police station reported the matter to the hospital. Detective Wu Changkai investigated and, in addition to reporting the case to the authorities to inspect the body and order its burial, police lawyer Wang Yaotang filed a public prosecution against the midwife Liu Wangshi. The First Special District Court held two hearings. Because the deceased Bao Huiying was short of funds after the abortion, she wrote a letter to Chen Weida, the owner of the Weida Hotel, a native of Nanhui, on March 8, asking for a loan. It was instructed to summon Chen to court for questioning. As reported previously, yesterday morning, Judge Qian Hongye resumed the trial of the defendant Liu Wangshi. Chen Weida and Bao Zhenyuan, the father of the deceased, appeared in court one after the other. Chen detailed the circumstances of the deceased's request for a loan in her letter, saying that he occasionally visited dance halls for social interaction with friends and had danced with the deceased. He only knew that they shared the same surname Bao, but he did not know her name. He had only met her in the dance hall and there was no further relationship. He had not seen her recently and had no impression of her in his mind. However, on the night of March 8, he suddenly received a letter delivered by a postman. When he opened it, he realized that it was from the dancer, asking to borrow dozens of yuan to meet an urgent need. He thought it was a common request for help and set it aside. Unexpectedly, on the night of the 11th, a police detective came to investigate, and he learned that the dancer had died from an abortion. Her father, Bao Zhenyuan, had even claimed at the police station that he had instigated the abortion, which was extremely absurd. Therefore, he immediately brought the letter he had received to the police station, where the police chief carefully examined it and determined that he had no connection with the abortion. With the truth clarified, Bao Zhenyuan begged him to give him some financial assistance because of his poverty. Originally, helping the poor and providing emergency relief was something that should be done, but if he had given him assistance at that time, he would have given others a reason to criticize him. Therefore, he refused to accommodate him. He then submitted the deceased's original letter to the court. After Judge Qian examined the letter, he stated that it was entirely a request for a loan from beginning to end, and that the beginning stated that they had not met for a long time, which proved that Bao's previous statement that his daughter had spoken to Chen on the phone on March 6 was unreliable. He then questioned Bao and the defendant Liu Wangshi. After the police lawyer concluded the debate, Judge Qian announced the verdict: Liu Wangshi, intending to make a profit, was entrusted by a pregnant woman to perform an abortion, resulting in death, is sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment, suspended for three years. As Chen Weida was only in the position of a witness, the court ordered him to leave after his testimony.

Chu Youliang Fraudulently Obtains Milk Money; Two Church Members Deceive the Priest; Furthermore, He Entices a Young Girl to Impersonate for Fraudulent Gain

Chu Yougen, a local resident residing at No. 11 Yugeng Lane, north of Meilong Town, Shanghai West (nicknamed "Little Limp"), is thirty years old, does not engage in legitimate work, and specializes in wandering aimlessly. Five years ago, he joined the Catholic Church in Xujiahui as a church member. The priest, considering his poverty, recommended him to work as a handyman in the Sacred Heart Hospital. In January of the 21st year of the Republic of China, Yougen took a baby girl who had been sheltered in the church for several months and ostensibly introduced her for milk feeding in the countryside (i.e., foster care) at three yuan per month, supplied by the church. In reality, Yougen sold the child to a neighboring woman named Chu (also known as Chu Ahu) in Dongyugeng Lane as an adopted daughter, obtaining six yuan. However, the child died of illness in June of the 22nd year of the Republic of China. Yougen concealed the report, and the milk money was still collected monthly. By January of this year, it had been three full years. According to the rules, the girl should be returned to the church, and he was repeatedly urged. Yougen made excuses to delay. At the end of last month, he had a strange idea. He tricked a three-year-old girl named A'mei, the daughter of his paternal uncle Chu Hegen, to the church in Xujiahui, claiming that each person could receive a reward of two yuan for vaccination. Hegen believed it to be true, so he entrusted Yougen to take the girl to Xujiahui for vaccination. Unexpectedly, Yougen left and never returned. Hegen's wife, Zhu, rushed to the Catholic Church the day before yesterday to inquire, only to find out that Yougen had used A'mei as the girl for milk feeding and received a reward of twelve yuan before fleeing without a trace. The priest of the church, upon learning of the previous situation, was greatly angered and has now reported to the Public Security Bureau and the British and French Concessions police to investigate and deal with it.

Husband Dies Five Days After Wedding

Widow Sues Father-in-Law for Alimony; Settlement Reached in Court

Peng Pinzhen, a woman from Songjiang, is twenty-two years old and a junior in high school at Aiguo Girls' School. She previously developed a romantic relationship with Gu Dicen, the son of Gu Hongxiang, a Jiaxing native residing at No. 8 Yuxiang Lane, Xiafei Road, French Concession, through friendship. Dicen is older than her by one year and has also received higher education. The engagement was arranged through matchmakers Zhang Yuquan and Gong Jingxiang. In September of last year, Dicen suddenly suffered from severe sleeping sickness. However, Miss Peng's love for Gu was profound. She deeply believed in the old custom that getting married during illness could bring about a turn for the better. Therefore, she had both families prepare for the wedding and carry it out. Unexpectedly, Gu Dicen died five days after the wedding, abandoning his beloved wife. Peng Pinzhen, having lost her husband at a young age, felt infinite pain in her spirit and was determined to remain chaste. Recently, she wanted to go abroad to study, hoping to gain profound knowledge in order to establish herself and make a living in the future. However, she could not obtain the understanding of her parents-in-law. Therefore, Peng Pinzhen hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit with the Civil Division of the Special Second Court, requesting a judgment ordering her father-in-law, Gu Hongxiang, to pay a lump sum of four thousand four hundred yuan for alimony, and to return her dowry. Based on the complaint, the court, through Judge Li Liang, summoned the plaintiff Peng Pinzhen and her lawyer to the court once to state the purpose of the request for judgment. The defendant, Gu Hongxiang, appeared in court through a lawyer and stated that the defendant only had one son, who unfortunately died early, causing him immense heartache. If his daughter-in-law could remain chaste, he, as an elder, would be able to find some comfort. However, the defendant did not agree with the plaintiff remaining chaste outside. If the defendant could study at home, the defendant could hire a teacher to teach her and did not want the plaintiff to go abroad to study. As for the plaintiff's request for living expenses, the bride's family had sixty acres of fertile land as dowry, which would not be a problem for the plaintiff's future life. The current lawsuit has other intentions. The court adjourned the hearing to summon the defendant again for questioning. Yesterday, it was time for the continued hearing. Both parties appeared in court with their lawyers and were still heard by Judge Li in the Civil Court No. 7. First, the plaintiff stated the purpose of the lawsuit, as before, requesting monthly living expenses of thirty yuan. The defendant stated that he was unable to bear the large amount of living expenses requested by the plaintiff because the property had already been mortgaged. At most, he could only afford to pay ten yuan per month for the plaintiff's living expenses. The official then summoned the two matchmakers, Zhang and Gong, for questioning and persuaded them to reconcile, asking both parties to compromise. The plaintiff then reduced the amount by five yuan, requesting at least twenty-five yuan per month. The defendant increased the amount by five yuan to fifteen yuan. After the court persuaded the defendant to pay twenty yuan per month, the plaintiff stated that it was not enough. After consultation between the lawyers of both parties, the defendant agreed to pay the plaintiff twenty-two yuan per month. With the plaintiff's permission, both parties reached a settlement in court, signed the minutes, and withdrew.

Municipal Health Bureau to Hold Regular Epidemic Prevention Campaign

The Municipal Health Bureau is paying close attention to the health of citizens. At that time, all municipal hospitals in the city will provide free vaccinations, and doctors will be dispatched to agencies and schools for vaccinations to prevent the spread of epidemic diseases.

All City Firefighters Participate in the Funeral Procession; Coffin to be Transported to Pudong for Burial

Jurisdiction Transferred; Debate Concluded in the Songhui Arson Case

Yin Shisheng, the former director of the Suzhou Public Security Bureau, opened the Songhui Amusement Park next to the Songhui Motor Road in his native Songjiang last summer. On July 15th and 16th, it was suddenly burned down. Yin Shisheng believed that Li Ruizhi and Yao Chongfu of the fire brigade in the area were involved. Based on the situation, he sued the Songjiang County Court and requested the Jiangsu High Court to transfer jurisdiction, designating the Shanghai District Court to handle the case. Prosecutor Kong Xianglin investigated and clarified the facts, ordering the two defendants, Li and Yao, to each pay a written surety of five hundred yuan to be released on bail pending further instructions. On one hand, they were prosecuted in the Criminal Court for offenses such as disrupting order, endangering public safety, and damaging public property. On the other hand, Yin Shisheng also filed an incidental private lawsuit, requesting compensation for losses of 18,477.66 yuan. Judge Shao Qinzhi held two public hearings, but the case was not concluded due to its complexity. Details were previously reported in the newspapers. It is now learned that the case was continued yesterday morning at 10 a.m. by Judge Shao. The plaintiff, Yin Shisheng, accompanied by his private lawsuit lawyer Cao Shouji, appeared in court to request the pursuit of the private lawsuit. The defendants, Li Ruizhi and Yao Chongfu, accompanied by their hired lawyers Jin Xiongbai, Yu Chuanding, Zhang Gugui, and Gu Changyuan, also attended the court one after another. After the interrogating official briefly questioned the two defendants, he ordered the debate to begin. The defendants' lawyers rose one after another to defend the defendants for a long time, mainly arguing that the two defendants did not incite the crowd to destroy the park. Moreover, they were doing things for the local public interest and would never do such a thing. Furthermore, the witnesses presented by the plaintiff, such as Inspector Wu Xisheng's report, stated that due to the large number of people (more than 10,000 people), it was difficult to identify the perpetrators, completely hoping to shift the blame to the fire brigade. The facts are clear. They requested that they be declared not guilty. The plaintiff stated that the people's houses, bedclothes, boxes, furniture, and other items were burned down, which was clearly witnessed by the patrolling officer Wu Xisheng (patrol leader Wu Qingzhen, etc., provided clear evidence in the investigation). The defendants should be held liable for the losses suffered by the people. After obtaining the testimony, the interrogating official ordered the debate to be concluded and scheduled the judgment to be pronounced at 2 p.m. on the 30th of this month. Each of the two defendants was given an additional surety of 2,000 yuan to be released on bail pending further instructions.
