Killed for a Boiler; Wang Wenyao's Skull Smashed and Killed

Wang Zuoju and His Gang Commit Murder; Men and Women Sent for Investigation

Jiang Laoba, the owner of a boiler shop at No. 208 Longhua Road, previously leased the boiler shop to Wang Zuoju for business because he did not intend to operate it. Recently, the lease term expired, and Jiang took back the shop and leased it to Wang Wenyao from Nanjing. As a result, Wang Zuoju was unemployed and had nothing to do. He suspected that Wang Wenyao was the one who caused trouble, so Jiang Laoba refused to extend the lease. The more he thought about it, the angrier he became, and the desire to kill arose in his heart. So, at around 7 p.m. on the 21st of this month, he gathered his nephew Wang Xiaoshand and others, including Fei Dequan, Wang Zhenbiao, Xu Dejin, and Tang Xiaowuzi, carrying axes and wooden sticks, and rushed to Wang Wenyao's house. Without asking any questions, they started to commit violence. Axes and sticks were wielded at the same time. Wang Wenyao was outnumbered, and his head was injured in three places by the axe. Bleeding profusely, he fell to the ground. When they saw that their goal had been achieved, they dispersed in a rush. Wang's wife, Yang, sent her husband to Shanghai Hospital for treatment and reported the incident to the police station in charge, who sent police to arrest Wang Zuoju, Fei Dejin, and Wang Zhenbiao's wife, Wang Zhang, and three other men and women to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation and detention. Unexpectedly, Wang Wenyao, who was injured, could not be saved due to brain damage. His condition worsened the night before last, and his breath was weak. He died soon after. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Zhao Chuanjia, commissioned by the court, and coroner Xuan Zhiming, etc., arrived at the court to examine the body. It was determined that the deceased Wang Wenyao died from his injuries. The death certificate was filled out, and the family members were ordered to prepare the coffin and wait for the police to send the criminals to court for interrogation and legal proceedings.

National Match Industry Association Submits Urgent Plea to Ministry of Finance Again for Relief

Match Industry Faces Perilous Situation, Imminent Collapse, Relief Urgently Requested to Alleviate Merchants' Hardships

The All-China Match Manufacturers' Association, previously due to falling market prices and declining business, submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance for relief. However, no concrete measures have been taken to date. Yesterday, the Association submitted another petition to the Ministry of Finance appealing for relief. The original text is as follows:

We, the association, reported in July of last year that the industry unanimously agreed that overproduction, business decline, and the sudden imposition of heavy taxes, made it increasingly difficult to prevent illicit leakage. The situation became increasingly perilous, and we requested that you forward our request and devise methods of relief. We thoroughly explained the reasons for the overproduction of matches and the difficulty of preventing illicit leakage. We also enclosed the "National Match Control Outline" and the "Match Joint Business Outline" approved by the Second Session of the Second Executive Committee of our association on December 10th of the previous year, together with various attachments, and submitted them to your ministry, requesting that you adopt and implement them to provide relief. Subsequently, we received document number 195 which stated that the submitted document and attachments had been received, and that the National Economic Council had been consulted for investigation and handling, and that we should be informed. After receiving this reply, our colleagues were overjoyed, believing that the fate of the match industry rested on this single opportunity, and eagerly awaited the realization of the control measures. However, many days have passed without any news. On the other hand, illicit leakage of matches has become increasingly active since the tax increase. Tax-paying matches are being heavily encroached upon, resulting in a narrower business scope, a deeper degree of overproduction, an imbalance between supply and demand, and more intense competition among our colleagues. Selling prices are gradually falling, costs can no longer be covered, high taxes cannot be passed on, and losses are increasing daily. The perilous situation is unprecedented, and we are barely clinging to life, facing imminent demise. Although our colleagues and the association have submitted reports to the Ministry of Finance and the Tax Affairs Department to order all bureaus to strictly crack down on illicit leakage, the great profits involved have attracted petty criminals who risk circumventing the law or taking advantage of loopholes. Various cunning schemes are being employed, which cannot be effectively addressed by ordinary anti-smuggling measures. If alternative relief measures are not sought, the trend of tax evasion will inevitably intensify. Not only will the match industry, which has been painstakingly developed for decades, be unable to survive due to the numerous obstacles, but also the various tax revenues of the country will be significantly affected. We believe that the preservation of industry to save the nation is the instruction left by Dr. Sun Yat-sen. However, when we consider the so-called emerging industries in our country, their lifelines are mostly controlled by foreigners. The match industry is one of the few industries that is 80% or 90% operated by Chinese people. This last remaining fruit of Chinese industry should be promptly assisted, otherwise its total destruction will deter Chinese people from investing in other enterprises and cause them to hesitate. Industry is linked to tax revenue. Assisting existing industries to maintain tax revenue is the best way to promote future industries and open up new tax sources. The matter is straightforward, and the principle is clear. Today, the match industry faces a perilous situation, with the constant threat of collapse. Providing relief as soon as possible still offers hope for survival. Delay will render even relief efforts futile. In the past, Bian Que told Duke Huan of Qi that if a disease is not treated when it is in the hair, it will penetrate deeper. The current condition of the match industry has progressed from the hair to the flesh, and is about to spread to the heart. The crisis is imminent, and we are on the verge of death. As a group representing this industry, and for the sake of the survival of our colleagues, we cannot but fulfill our responsibility to advocate and appeal. Your ministry, for the sake of national tax revenue and the future of industry in our country, will surely not stand idly by. We dare not hesitate to submit this urgent appeal. We earnestly implore your ministry to consider Dr. Sun Yat-sen's instructions to save the nation, to consider the precarious state of the match industry, and to promptly devise relief measures to alleviate the hardships of merchants and protect the foundation of the nation. We await your instructions with utmost urgency.

Resolution of Dispute at Huafeng Flour Mill

Regarding the work stoppage dispute at the Huafeng Flour Mill in Xiaoshadu, the Social Affairs Bureau convened both labor and management yesterday to conduct mediation. A resolution was reached: (1) Management will prepare to resume work, and before work resumes, management will be responsible for maintaining food for workers and staff; (2) Workers shall not obstruct the factory's goods, and management will find a way to clear the back wages owed for March. Both parties were satisfied with these two measures, and the dispute was resolved.

Shen Jiayi Practices Law

Mr. Shen Jiayi, courtesy name Yanmou, is a native of Tongxiang, Zhejiang. After graduating from the Shanghai Aurora University with a doctorate in law, he went to France for further studies. He later graduated with honors from the Paris School of Political Science in France. After returning to China, he served as a professor at the Shanghai Law School, Shanghai Political Science and Law School, Jinan University, National Business School, Fudan University, and as the Director of the Law Department of Xiamen University. He has written books such as "Guanzi's Political, Legal and Economic Theories" and "Commentary on the General Principles of Civil Law." His knowledge and experience are highly regarded by the times. Recently, he was encouraged by friends, and with the aim of serving society, he joined the Bar Association and set up an office on the fourth floor of the Dafeng Dyeing and Weaving Company at 349 Ningbo Road to practice law. It is believed that Mr. Shen, with his concern for the protection of human rights, will be able to benefit society. This is recorded here to inform all sectors.

Letters to the Editor

I recently read your newspaper's fourth page, thirteenth edition, which contained an article titled "Firefighter Dies in the Line of Duty." The content does not align with the facts. Upon investigation, the fire originated in a corner of the Tongchang Yarn Factory workshop, adjacent to our factory, not within our premises. When the fire started, our factory promptly used its own firefighting equipment to extinguish it. By the time the fire brigade arrived, the fire was already put out. Only a few dozen cotton yarn cones were burned; the building's bricks and tiles sustained no damage. Fearing external misunderstandings, we are writing to request a correction. Jin Cheng Bank 1934 Business Report (11)

Average Monthly Export Trade Volume of Soviet Russia

Average Monthly Trade Deficit (--) or 13.58 -1.88 -14.49 -10.76 +12.29 +14.55

Surplus (+)

Average for January to September

B. Domestic Economic Overview: During the initial two years of the global economic depression, China's situation differed significantly from other countries, experiencing relatively minimal impact. China was fortunate to avoid the worst of the crisis temporarily because it operated on a silver standard. The ratio of silver to gold depreciated at a rate equal to or exceeding the depreciation of commodity prices calculated in gold. As a result, Chinese commodity prices sometimes remained constant or even increased due to the low silver price. Foreign trade was more profitable due to the gold price. Although reduced foreign purchasing power led to a slight decline in export trade, it was not as severe as in other countries. Domestic industries were also able to maintain a normal level of activity. Therefore, the gradual decline in the price of silver during those two years greatly benefited China. However, starting in September 1931, countries such as Britain, Japan, and the United States successively abandoned the gold standard. China's currency gradually appreciated due to these changes, and China also began to fall into the economic difficulties experienced by other countries. In this year, the country was plagued by floods and droughts, and affected by the United States' silver policy. The malaise of the rural areas deepened, and the industry and commerce of the cities declined. The purchasing power of the general public decreased. Our country's economic problems are increasingly watched by all parties.

(1) Finance: This year, China's financial situation showed an unusual phenomenon, namely the large export of silver, the low deposit reserve of foreign banks in Shanghai, and the insignificant decrease in the deposit reserve of Chinese banks. First, the situation of silver import and export is listed in the following table: (To be continued)

Datong University Adds a Physical Education Department

Datong University's physical education facilities have always been known for their completeness. In recent years, it has vigorously implemented popular physical education and has actively expanded. The area of the sports field reaches more than 80 acres, which is especially rare. There is also a river of more than 60 acres in the school. The river water is clear and can be used for swimming and boating. The school's directors, He Yingqin, Chu Minyi, and Wu Tiecheng, are all very enthusiastic about promoting physical education. Therefore, at the spring board meeting this year, it was proposed to add a physical education department. It was unanimously approved by all the directors, and Wang Boqun, the president of the school, hired the current director of physical education at the school, Fang Wanbang, a Master of Physical Education from Columbia University in the United States, who has served as a physical education professor at Beijing Normal University, Anhui University, National Central University, and Zhejiang University, as the director. Mr. Fang carefully planned and formulated the curriculum, and decided to start it in the autumn, recruiting high school graduates, and giving them two years of specialized physical education knowledge and skills. Men and women will be trained in separate classes, in order to cultivate appropriate physical education teachers for primary and secondary schools, physical education administrators, and scout leaders. The school's College of Education has a long-standing reputation, and the science department is also very well-equipped. Students of the physical education department can study courses related to physical education at the same time as students in the university department, such as the principles of education, educational administration, teaching methods, psychology, physiology, and hygiene. All the excellent facilities and teaching materials in the school can be used as much as possible, which is a rare opportunity.

Japanese Police Bureau Decides to Adopt Confucian and Mencian Teachings as Educational Policy

Does Japan really respect the teachings of Confucius and Mencius?

The World News Agency said, according to the Dongbao report, the Police Bureau under the Ministry of Interior has now decided to implement a new educational policy for all police schools in the country, that is, to use the teachings of Confucius and Mencius as the basic education, in order to promote the Eastern way of governing the country and bringing peace to the world. On the one hand, the original courses in international law and other laws will be completely abolished or reduced, because these subjects are considered to be of little use to future police maintenance. It is found that the intention of this policy change of the Police Bureau is to focus on cultivating the moral heart of police officers, and regards knowledge as secondary. This new policy will be implemented from April 1, and the bureau will also compile and print a periodical to clarify the purpose of this, in order to control all 63,000 active police officers in the country with this new policy.

Chen Heqin's Talk on Phonetic Notation of Chinese Characters

This newspaper reported on the 13th of this month that Li Jinxi responded to Shu Xincheng's discussion on casting copper molds for phonetic notation of Chinese characters. Educator Chen Heqin expressed his opinion on this matter, stating briefly that the language in the newspaper was not detailed. However, after examining the wording, it seems that he does not advocate replacing Chinese characters with phonetic symbols, but rather proposes using symbols to indicate the correct pronunciation so that readers do not suffer the hardship of not being able to pronounce the characters. Regarding this point, I believe that compiling a correct national pronunciation dictionary for primary school teachers to follow and for students to consult on their own is sufficient to fulfill its mission. As for the plan to print all popular reading materials and primary school textbooks in phonetic notation of Chinese characters, it seems largely unnecessary. Forcibly implementing it may lead to the following drawbacks:

(1) Time-consuming: Although phonetic symbols alongside characters are necessary for new words, the number of new words in each lesson is extremely limited. If all familiar words that have already been read are also marked with phonetic notation, students will inevitably spend more effort on their eyesight when reading. Moreover, characters and symbols placed together can easily confuse the vision and distract attention, making teaching time-consuming, which goes without saying.

(2) Eye strain: Children's eyesight is not as good as adults'. With the current font size of textbooks, reading can sometimes be difficult. Adding phonetic symbols would make it even more difficult to see clearly, causing eye strain and easily leading to the danger of nearsightedness, which is very concerning.

(3) Prone to errors: Since it is not easy to see clearly, the chance of errors is bound to increase. Furthermore, with characters and symbols mixed together, young children may easily mistake the symbols as part of the characters, leading to errors.

(4) Research should be conducted first: In the United States, the difficulty of reading text is tested in detail using photographic methods, and the results are very good. The matter of phonetic notation of Chinese characters is of great importance. It is best for domestic universities or specialized educational institutions to test and research it first before considering implementation. Otherwise, it may not only be of little benefit, but may even be harmful.

Special Article

German Science and Chinese Books (Part 2)

— By Dr. Jieqin, German Library Committee

Regarding Shanghai, the Mutual Aid Association also donated a portion of its industrial books to Jiaotong University and books on national economics to the Business School of Central University. At the same time, it established close ties with Fudan University, Tongji University, and other research laboratories. Tongji University received special attention from the Mutual Aid Association and was regularly assisted. Although the internal economic situation in Germany was very difficult, it still spared no expense in donating valuable first editions to Tongji University.

The Mutual Aid Association has had relations with the Academia Sinica for several years. Recently, the Mutual Aid Association published a lengthy report, aiming to inform Germans about the Mutual Aid Association's collaborative experiment, an experiment to systematize China's scientific life. While striving to establish relations with various aspects of China, the Mutual Aid Association also hopes to establish similar relations with libraries, so that every interaction becomes a mutual interaction. This is what this article should explain.

The German Academic Mutual Aid Association's assistance to libraries is not like that of Americans, who focus solely on appearances. The will of the German Academic Mutual Aid Association is to enrich the content of Chinese libraries by donating German books to Chinese libraries or using them to exchange for Chinese books. It would be a great honor to receive book donations from the Chinese side.

Regarding Beiping, the former capital of China, the Mutual Aid Association has long established close ties with the Beiping Library. The books donated by the Mutual Aid Association to the library include the great works of botanist Landolt-Bornstein and books on subjects such as geography and archaeology. In addition, a considerable number of books on German language and literature have also been donated. In Beiping, the Mutual Aid Association also established complex relationships with other parties through the library's introduction, such as the libraries of Yenching University, Peking University, Tsinghua University, the Beiping Research Institute, National University, the Central Observatory, and the Catholic University of Peking.

Similar relationships also exist in Guangzhou, especially with the library and the university of Sun Yat-sen University. Other institutions and schools, such as Lingnan University, professors, and private individuals, such as Professor Wang, also have close relationships. However, the Mutual Aid Association's relationships with Beiping and Guangzhou are almost entirely based on exchange.

Wuhan, located in the center of the Yangtze River, has also established a relationship with the Mutual Aid Association because the association collected a large number of German books for Wuhan University. The books for Wuhan University were donated by German Ambassador to China Dr. Trautmann in his personal capacity, and they include books on biographies, history, law, ancient works, physics, and chemistry.

In Nanjing, the Mutual Aid Association is currently very close to Mr. Jiang Fuzong of the National Central Library. The Central University Library and the National Government Health Administration also have considerable connections. In addition, Zhejiang University and Zhejiang Provincial Library in Hangzhou, and the University of Hong Kong and the Royal Research Institute in Hong Kong are also related to the Mutual Aid Association.

It would be too verbose to list all the institutions, schools, and groups in China that have relationships with the Mutual Aid Association. However, if other libraries that were not originally related need assistance from the Mutual Aid Association after reading this article, the association will certainly not spare any effort or avoid any difficulties to provide assistance, in order to gain the sympathy and mutual aid of the other party.

Children's Weekly

Little Scientist

— Bai Tao

The modern child is a little scientist. Little scientists engage in small experiments, small reforms, and small inventions. They want to play active games and not read dead science textbooks.

Of course, little scientists also need to use books, but they use living books: mountains, rivers, grass, trees, insects, birds, fish, and beasts are living books; clouds, rain, wind, snow, the sun, moon, stars, the vastness of the universe, and the smallness of microorganisms are all living books.

The entire universe is the science textbook used by little scientists, and it is also the little scientists' great laboratory. To obtain true knowledge and to unlock all the mysterious riddles of nature, one must make active use of these books in the great laboratory.

In fact, children are born as little scientists in this large laboratory. When the sky thunders, they ask, "Why is that?" When spiders eat mosquitoes, they watch and ask, "What are they doing?" And the famous great scientists and great inventors in the world have all used these living books and honed their skills in this great laboratory. For example, Darwin, Newton, and Galileo are good examples. Therefore, little scientists are promising great scholars and great inventors of the future, as long as you children do not forget these precious living books and this great laboratory.

Literary Stories

— Sun Yucai

(1) National Hero Shi Dakai

Shi Dakai was a famous general of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom. He was not only proficient in military affairs but also deeply versed in literature. At that time, the generals were fighting for power and killing each other. Shi Dakai saw that this emerging revolutionary government would not work, so he led a troop alone and went straight to Sichuan, intending to launch another major offensive. Unfortunately, he could not support himself alone and eventually failed. According to the official report, Shi Dakai was captured and killed by Qing soldiers after his defeat; but according to unofficial history, Shi Dakai was not captured, nor was he killed. Indeed, such a national hero, we do not want him to be harmed.

Now, let's just talk about one of his stories; for some reason, his enemy Zeng Guofan also fell in love with his talent and wrote letters to persuade him to surrender. A revolutionary like Shi Dakai would certainly not be recruited by Zeng Guofan, the representative of feudalism. He wrote four poems and gave him a stern refusal. Two lines in the poem read:

"My ambition is unfulfilled, and people are suffering; there are tears everywhere in the southeast."

From these two lines, we can see his concern for the people's suffering and his true revolutionary colors. Not to mention that none of the generals at that time had such a benevolent heart, but even in modern times, it is not common.

(2) Nian Gengyao Asks About Characters

Nian Gengyao was a great general of the Qing Dynasty who once conquered Tibet, pacified the Sichuan border, and quelled Qinghai. His achievements were great.

It is said that he was very smart when he was young. His father hired several teachers to teach him at home, but none of the teachers were not embarrassed by him and willingly resigned.

Once, his father hired a very famous local teacher to teach him. On the first day of school, Nian Gengyao wrote the character "重" (chóng, heavy) and asked the teacher, "How do you explain this character '重'?"

"The character '重' means not light," the teacher replied.

"Wrong, wrong, if you break the character '重' apart, it is the character for "thousand" 千 and "li" 里, obviously it means very far, how can you say it means not light?" Nian Gengyao said with a smile.

The teacher's face flushed red, and he remained silent.

The next day, Nian Gengyao wrote the character "矮" (ǎi, short) and "射" (shè, shoot) and asked the teacher, "How do you explain these two characters?"

"The character '矮' means not tall, so people who are not tall are called dwarfs; the character '射' means to shoot an arrow," the teacher replied.

"According to your explanation, it is wrong. In my opinion, the characters '矮' and '射' should be switched around. You see, the character '射' is composed of the characters for "inch" 寸 and "body" 身, if a person's body is only one inch, wouldn't that be short? As for the character '矮', it is clearly composed of the characters for "arrow" 矢 and "abandon" 委, abandoning an arrow means shooting an arrow, right?" Nian Gengyao said with a hearty laugh.

"The way the Chinese create characters is really upside down. For example, the characters '牛' (niú, cow) and '魚' (yú, fish) should also be switched around," Nian Gengyao continued.

"What is the reason for this?" the teacher asked in surprise.

"The character '魚' clearly resembles a four-legged animal, while the character '牛' is just a water animal with a head, tail, and no feet, so why is it upside down?" Nian Gengyao said.

The teacher felt that Nian Gengyao's talent was truly extraordinary and that he did not have the talent to teach him. He thought about it all night in bed, and as soon as the east turned white, he resigned and left.

Suffering and Joy

— Kang Jianzhaifu

Poor children,

How bitter!

Barefoot, rags all over.

Collecting firewood, picking dung, doing everything,

Hands like iron rakes, face like soil.

Eating coarse vegetable roots to fill their stomachs,

Relying entirely on hard work to overcome difficulties!

Poor children,

Don't refuse suffering!

Rich children,

How joyful!

Fine clothes, delicious food, everything is sufficient.

Sitting and eating, the mountains will be emptied, and the sea will dry up,

No matter how much gold and jade are hidden in your home!

You should know the difficulty of every thread and every stitch,

You must learn every talent and skill.

Rich children,

Don't be greedy for joy!

The Old Hen

— Lin Yin

The old hen was clucking, feeling that her life was very pitiful, not having laid many eggs to keep her company in her loneliness. She clucked like this everywhere in the cool air: "Cluck, cluck, so lonely! Cluck, cluck, so lonely!"

One day, she hatched several eggs from the grass nest. She was very happy, now she could hatch chicks to comfort her loneliness. She immediately arranged the grass pile into a nest like the one she lived in. She put the eggs in the middle of the grass nest and carefully squatted on top of the eggs. She covered the eggs with her wings and patiently waited for the chicks to hatch from the eggshells. She thought: Sweet days are coming soon.

Days passed, and today was the third Sunday after the hen began incubating the eggs. The old hen's clucking already sounded very happy and joyful. She gently tucked her wings in, and immediately heard "peeping" sounds from inside the eggshells. The old hen was really extremely happy. She clucked: "Cluck, cluck, so happy! Cluck, cluck, so happy!"

The hen's hope was realized, and chicks hatched from all the eggshells. The old hen took them out to look for food. She clucked all the way, and the chicks gathered around her. But she was very strange, why didn't the chicks look like her at all. Their mouths were flat, their bodies were long, their legs were short, and even their calls were "Xi ya," "Xi ya." This could not help but make the old hen suspicious.

They walked to the pond, and the old hen was about to teach them how to peck at food, but the group of children all jumped into the pond! The old hen cried out anxiously: "Cluck, cluck! Come and save them! Cluck, cluck! Come and save them!" The old duck heard the cries and quickly ran to the pond. The old hen shouted: "Cluck, cluck! The children are about to drown!" The old duck laughed loudly, "Gak, gak, gak! These are my children!" It also quickly jumped into the water.

The old hen stared blankly at them, only to see them swimming happily in the water. She had to walk back to the grass nest, clucking, clucking.

How Plants Defend Themselves

— Dong Chuncai

Whether plants or animals, they all have natural self-defense abilities. Like animals and humans, plants also have many enemies and dangers. In this natural world of the survival of the fittest, those plants that cannot defend themselves will eventually perish, only those that are strong can survive.

Many insects, fish, birds, and beasts can harm plants. Plants must defend themselves to survive. Of course, plants cannot fight enemies like animals: they cannot run away either: but they do have many self-defense methods to resist those greedy enemies.

Some plants have a foul odor, and few animals want to eat them; some plants have poisonous juices, which make herbivores who want to eat them not dare to try; some plants have a sour, astringent, or spicy taste, which makes people not dare to try a second time after tasting it once. Although some plants do not have foul odors, some animals like to eat them, but most herbivores know not to patronize them.

Plants defend themselves against enemies, not only by using unpleasant odors. Many plants are born with self-defense weapons, such as thorns, and if animals try to bite them, their mouths will be pierced. Some plants have stiff hairs to resist those greedy snails. Some plants can secrete mucus to defend against insect attacks.

Regarding plant self-defense, we may as well cite an example to illustrate. Mint has a special fragrance, and we often use it as a medicine, but herbivorous animals are very afraid of its scent. Rhododendron, Rhododendron mucronatum, etc., are all poisonous plants, and herbivorous animals do not dare to taste them.

The fruits of chestnuts are covered with thorns: hawthorns and the stems of trifoliate orange have thorns; barberry leaves also have spines below: the stems and leaves of thistles are covered with thorns: the edges of catbrier leaves have needle-like serrations: herbivores do not dare to touch these thorny plants. The buds of horse chestnuts and the stems of catchflies can secrete mucus to defend against insect attacks. The branches and leaves of nettles have stiff hairs and contain venom. If you are not careful and touch it, its stiff hairs will pierce your skin and inject the venom into your blood, which is quite painful.

Although plants have various self-defense methods, some animals can still harm them. However, there are very few animals that dare to oppose plants that have bad odors and thorns. Only a few animals dare to invade them; then, they will be very dominant in the struggle for survival.

Story Picture

— Zhang Youjian

—Going to the Sea—

(1) Rong'er took a fishing rod and stood on the edge of the boat to fish.

(2) The cook in the cabin was cutting up a big fish: suddenly, a fishing hook flew in through the window and happened to hook the fish's mouth.

(3) Rong'er pulled up the fishing rod; unexpectedly, he hooked a big fish without a tail.

(4) Fei'er saw this and wanted to take it and cook it himself, so he pretended to be horrified and said, "This was caught from the cabin, it should be returned to him, let me take it to return it to him." After speaking, he snatched the big fish and fishing rod from Rong'er's hands.

(5) The cook took the remaining tail to compare, and this fish was indeed his own. But Fei'er refused to return it to him and wanted to run away.

(6) The cook was extremely angry and kicked Fei'er away, and Fei'er fell head over heels into the sea.

Problems with Children's Books

— Huang Yide

"The new discovery of the 24th century is the discovery of children." Since this saying came out, it seems that our Chinese children's education has gradually become more valued. At the same time, our publishing industry, in recent years, the publication of children's books has been like "bamboo shoots after a rain."

This cannot be said to be anything but a blessing for Chinese children.

But Chinese children are unfortunately Chinese children. China is a China burdened with national humiliation, a China weak in the state and poor in the people, a China backward in everything: the problem of children's books in such a country is indeed a serious problem and it is not just publishing a little children's reading material that can be considered helpful for children's education or a contribution to children's culture.

You come up with a set of children's libraries, and I also come up with a set of children's libraries; you publish 200 copies of children's reading materials, and I publish 300 copies of children's reading materials. Is this competition for culture? Is this competition for business? Not to mention that, "the more the better," the phenomenon is good. Chinese education has not been popularized yet, and after education is universal, publishing thousands of copies, tens of thousands of copies, and hundreds of thousands of copies is not too much. But the most important issue is that fewer "children's reading materials" should be published, and more "children's textbooks" should be published. "Children's reading materials" are passive, while "children's textbooks" are active. Children in such a country do not need passive "reading materials" to read casually, but rather active "textbooks" to do things with their own hands. Because the children of such a China really don't have the leisure to read idle books, and really don't have the money to buy idle books!

Then what kind of textbooks should be given to children in such a country? This is one of the tasks that this association -- the Chinese Children's Culture Association -- should work hard on. We hope that people from all walks of life, school teachers, and family parents can give us assistance.

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (II)

— Xin Qing

The captain came up to me and said, "I have a package of goods that a man brought on board with us when we set sail. Now that he is dead, I want to sell these goods and pay the money to his descendants. If you are willing to accept it and sell it for me, then after you sell it, I will give you some money to reward you for your labor."

I was happy to do this, because I like to work. Then the captain called the ship's clerk to make a list of the packages I received.

He said, "Write it down in the name of Sinbad the Sailor."

When I heard these words, my heart was filled with joy. Then I let the captain know who I was, because he thought I was dead. At first, he didn't remember.

It's no wonder he didn't know me, because my recent life had changed me a lot.

You all must think that I should have recognized him immediately, but I must tell you that he was the leader of the ship on my second voyage, and it had been a very, very long time since I last saw him.

I said, "I am that Sinbad, whom you previously left on that island. At that time, I fell asleep by a stream, but when I woke up, I saw that the ship had gone far away."

The captain said, "Ah! I recognize you now! I cannot say due to what unfortunate circumstances you were left on the island. At that time, all of us had returned to the ship, but I didn't know you were missing. When a strong wind blew up, we realized you were no longer on board, but we couldn't sail back."

I was very happy to see him make good sales of my goods in various ports, so he handed over the money and goods to me.

We sailed from Sabella Island to a place where I accumulated various precious spices.

Here I saw many strange things, some looking like a cow with a fish's tail, a huge turtle, and many other things.

After some time, we arrived at Balsara, and from there we set off for Baghdad, at which time we arrived in this town. I was now very rich, and everything I owned was countless. I gave a large sum of money to the poor, and in addition to what I already owned, I bought many properties.

Spring Bees

— Zou Xiao

Little friends, now as long as you are willing to go to the countryside for a stroll, you can see all kinds of flowers, red, yellow, purple, white... everywhere, east and west, the thriving scene is really a pleasure to see. And those groups of bees, you can see them everywhere, flying east for a while, flying west for a while, how beautiful!

Little friends, do you think that those groups of bees are just playing in the countryside? If you think so, then you are wronging them. They are not playing, they are actually working hard at their proper work! What work are they doing? Do you all understand?

They are all doing the work of "collecting flowers and making honey"!

They can work hard, so they can produce sweet sugar. The sugar they make is so sweet, and after this season of hard work, their food for the whole year is prepared, so they will never suffer from hunger! Little friends, have you heard the news of bees starving to death? I can tell you for sure that they won't. Because they are all willing to work hard!

Little friends, you are like them in this spring when you are young, so now that they are working so hard, how should you work hard at this time so as not to be ashamed of them? I hope you will work even harder than them!

However, the current demand from yarn buyers is weaker than before, but some anticipate a return to bullish conditions.

U.S. Cotton Rises Sharply Against Short Positions

—Rebounds by 20-30 Points—

Yesterday, the U.S. cotton after-hours market was firm. Until noon, the March contract fell due to delivery notices reaching 7,800 bales, mostly absorbed by spot traders. There were few sellers, and trading houses continued to enter the market. Japanese buyers purchased old cotton, while new buyers were scarce. Trading houses awaited developments in Washington. Later, news that the House of Representatives had passed the Patman Bonus Bill caused short positions to cover, and the market turned firm. Simultaneously, rising wheat and stocks also boosted cotton market sentiment. Hester estimated factory consumption for the week at 263,000 bales, and Liverpool inventories at 307,000 bales. The closing trend was very bullish, with spot prices rising by 25 points and futures by 23 to 34 points. English spot cotton fell by 5 points, while futures rose by 3 points. Indian cotton initially weakened due to short selling and long liquidation, but later firmed due to good spot demand and commercial buying. Pingle rose by 4.5 rupees, Oomra by 5.75 rupees, and Bai Luo Creek by 1.75 rupees. The original telegram records are as follows (dated the 23rd):

U.S. Cotton Fell Sharply Last Week Due to the European Situation

A telegram from New York on the 22nd reported on the cotton market for the week: At the beginning of the week, the market fell sharply again due to long liquidation and the resumption of hedging, to protect inventories or cotton in storage. Furthermore, the European political situation was chaotic, and foreign exchange rates were unstable. Later, short covering and buying by trading houses stemmed the decline, but with sluggish demand, prices fluctuated up and down. It was reported that Southern senators supported the government's continued loan policy and the encouragement of export sales, as well as the elimination of the continued tax, which triggered a rebound. Market participants are awaiting the authorities' actions. The House of Representatives passed a provision in the Penhale Act to exempt farmers from taxes on the production of three bales, which may face strong opposition. The spot market shows no signs of softening. Hedging was minimal after the decline on Monday.

Grains: Foreign Wheat Rises; Flour Wheat Soars

—Bran Market Shows Little Movement—

After the opening of the flour market this morning, all months showed a sharp rise. Foreign wheat quotations showed a Chicago increase of approximately 24 points and a Canadian increase of 0.10 yuan. At the opening, foreign wheat continued to rise. Furthermore, due to the turmoil in Eastern Europe and the fear of an outbreak, this situation is currently not of great concern. However, imports of wheat from the East may inevitably be affected. Therefore, both industry insiders and external buyers were active, and market sentiment gradually rose. Compared to the opening, the current month's market saw a slight easing of customer demand, and the trend was peaceful. For the deferred months, external investors bought in, and it was reported that Nanyang trading houses also purchased a significant amount. However, large factories sold off. Nevertheless, confidence remained as strong as ever. As a result, the current month rose by 0.015 yuan, April by 0.0275 yuan, May by 0.04 yuan, June by 0.045 yuan, and July/August by 0.0525 yuan.

After the opening of the wheat market this morning, all months showed a uniformly firm trend. Foreign wheat quotations showed a Chicago increase of approximately 24 points and a Canadian increase of 0.10 yuan. At the opening, all months showed positive signs, and foreign wheat continued to rise. Furthermore, the serious situation in Eastern Europe boosted previously subdued confidence. Therefore, both near-term and distant-term asking prices were uniformly high, rising by 0.03 to 0.05 yuan compared to the previous day. At the afternoon opening, trading in all months remained stable, with confidence even stronger in distant months. Generally, people fear that foreign wheat may be affected. As a result, the current month rose by 0.03 yuan, July by 0.06 yuan, and August by 0.05 yuan. The spot wheat market remained stable. High-quality wheat saw a slight increase of 0.01 to 0.02 yuan, while medium-quality wheat remained unchanged. Anhui Su County wheat was priced at 3.66 yuan, Shandong wheat at 3.64 yuan, and Bengbu wheat at 3.59 yuan, with a total of 1,500 bags purchased by Fuxin.

Rice Market Continues to Decline

The rice market has been reporting frequent declines in prices due to abundant inventories. The market was unable to change yesterday. The details are as follows:

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, over 20 shipments arrived from various trading houses, totaling nearly 4,000 shi (a unit of dry measure). Both wholesale and retail markets were flat. The market was high in the morning and weak in the afternoon. Prices for high-quality and medium-quality japonica and thin indica rice fell by several cents to nearly a jiao (a unit of currency), while Du Jian rice also softened. Due to limited sales, Yin Bian Yuan rice continued to fall by about a jiao.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, over 40 boats arrived from various trading houses in the lower reaches of the river. Sales in the market were flat. Prices for high-quality white japonica rice fell by 0.05 to 0.06 yuan, medium-quality rice by slightly over 0.10 yuan, and top-quality Yang Jian and top-quality Bian Yuan rice by slightly over a jiao. Early thin indica rice prices fell by several cents, while other rice showed a softening trend.

(Imported Rice) Demand from customers was weak, and the market turned flat and soft. However,囤戶 (speculators) believe that the situation in Eastern Europe is becoming increasingly urgent, and that the grain market may tighten in the future. Therefore, they are no longer eager to sell. However, demand from local customers is also weak, and the market is difficult to improve. The total daily volume was only around 5,000 bags, distributed to inland areas by local merchants.

(Hakka Xian Rice) After the price drop the day before, sales remained strong yesterday. However, inland trading houses were very price-sensitive. Although trading was active yesterday, prices continued to be flat and soft. Over 3,000 bags were sold throughout the city, all of which were purchased by inland buyers.

(Soybeans) Due to sluggish sales, the market was flat and long, with short-term activity. Two cars of Yingzhou soybeans were opened at a price of 3.50 yuan and 3.54 yuan, respectively. One car of Bengbu soybeans was priced at 3.40 yuan. Two cars of Dalian Siping Street soybeans were priced at 4.10 yuan and 4.08 yuan, respectively. Over 700 bags of Hankou soybeans were priced from 3.47 yuan to 3.22 yuan.

Silk and Tea: Needle Eyebrow Tea Sales Still Strong

In the local tea market, sales to foreign merchants have remained stagnant in recent days. However, northern trading houses from Tianjin and Shandong require large quantities of Needle and Eyebrow green teas, as spring sales have already begun. Over 700 boxes of each type of tea were purchased from various tea shops in the past two days. Needle Eyebrow tea was priced at 15 to 16 yuan, and Eyebrow tea at 11 yuan. The tea will be shipped for export soon. British firms such as Jardine Matheson and Yieh Hwa have also sent telegrams to reduce prices and promote sales of Zhen Mei green tea and Hubei red tea.

Sugar Market: Domestically Produced Coarse White Sugar Rises Another 0.20 Yuan

Re-exported Dutch Coarse White Sugar Up 0.30 Yuan

Yesterday, the sugar market continued to show a tight trend. The potential implementation of tariffs on foreign sugar kept sentiment bullish. The Sugar Association raised the single-sale price of high-quality domestically produced Guangdong coarse white sugar by 0.20 yuan to 17.20 yuan. High-quality and secondary-grade sugars were priced at a 0.10 yuan increase from the previous day's listed prices, to 17.10 yuan, 17.00 yuan, and 16.90 yuan, respectively. The price of re-exported 24 Dutch coarse white sugar rose even more sharply, increasing by another 0.30 yuan to 5.20 yuan. It was rumored that off-exchange prices were even higher. Due to rising raw material prices, local factories were unable to continue production of refined white sugar, resulting in a temporary lack of supply. Taikoo sugar was priced at 18.00 yuan, an increase of 0.30 to 0.40 yuan. Chaozhou traders offered the original 150 bags of crystal sugar at 13.00 yuan, 100+ bags from Hainan at 10.05 yuan, and 100+ bags from Huanggang Qing at 9.00 to 9.90 yuan, with little difference from previous prices. Huilai sold 200 bags of raw sugar at 9.50 to 9.55 yuan, an increase of 0.10 yuan.

Hardware: Hooping Tinplate Sells Well

Hooping tinplate is a popular product in the tinplate market because its use is more economical than standard tinplate. Additionally, cigarette factories must use it to make large boxes. As such, market demand is quite strong. Recently, due to limited arrivals and low inventories, prices have risen slightly. It is estimated that each 200-pound bundle is worth 24 yuan, an increase of 1 yuan from the previous day. It is reported that trading houses such as Xietai, Fuji, and Ni Jingji have a strong demand for this product. Unfortunately, few traders in the market hold this product, resulting in very tight prices.

Blue Lead is Being Hoarded for Speculation

Blue lead trading has increased slightly recently. Overseas prices have increased sharply, so wealthy financial firms have begun hoarding. Brokers have been scouring the market for several days, and over 3,000 bars were sold yesterday. The lack of freely circulating goods has resulted in another 0.15 yuan increase in price. The estimated value is 13.90 yuan.

Refined Antimony Falls Again by Over 10 Yuan

There are few transactions in refined antimony, and prices are very soft. It is estimated that each ton is worth 760 yuan, a decrease of approximately 15 yuan from the previous day. Transactions were limited to small purchases and sales, with no large-scale negotiations. It is reported that there are many arrivals from the production areas. Market sentiment is weak, and future market prices are likely to fall more than they rise.
