Women's World

Haste and Confusion

—Bi Wu

Just as adults and gentlemen were engaged in high-sounding discussions over tea and wine about "Women Returning to the Home," news of women's suicides flew in daily like snowflakes: this silent, concrete response was terribly bleak and cruel!

In recent days, in addition to a series of suicide reports, suddenly came the shocking national Liu Jinggui murder case: suicide, murder, the Chinese women's world of 1935 is almost slaughtered into pieces. But in this bloody and bitter atmosphere, there are also some funny, laughable materials, the most prominent of which is the propaganda of a certain Yao transforming from a woman into a man.

Why are there so many tricks in today's female world? What is the common thread among these tricks?

Suicide, many people already think, is the behavior of the weak, while murder, on the other hand, should be considered the behavior of the strong. But not necessarily. Looking at Liu Jinggui's remarks: "I came here today specifically to beat Teng Shuang, because her husband 'Ji Jiong Ming' was my former fiancé. Originally, her husband deceived me, and I originally intended to beat her husband to death, but because I could not achieve it, I beat her to death." This statement is very clear: Liu Jinggui, who committed murder, was also a weak woman, excessively angered by oppression.

As for a certain Yao, a woman who falsely claims to have become a man, this is because most people still think that men are superior to women, and that if a woman can transform into a man, then that person must have a special, heaven-moving sincerity, and only then will this result occur. Therefore, a certain Yao's trick is precisely the desperate trick of a weak woman when she has no other choice.

When weak women reach a dead end, they resort to suicide, or murder, or prostitution, or playing tricks.

How can she be so weak? Because she has no power, no social status, no hope, and is given only a narrow home and the status of a slave. She sees everything in the world as empty, and all money, power, art, and fame do not belong to her. The most real and most important thing she sees is herself. For the sake of her own problems, she can abandon herself to suicide, or abandon herself to murder, or abandon herself to playing other tricks. Moreover, in her situation, even if she does not abandon herself, society sometimes forces her to do so.

The increasing number of unfortunate events in the women's world recently demonstrates that women's status in society is becoming weaker. "Women Return to the Home!" The revival of the good wife and wise mother ideology has increased her new, heavier burden than in previous years, and stripped away the small amount of hope for liberation she had before. In life and in thought, she is only given blows and not a bright way out. She can only stumble and stumble blindly.

However, "a hungry person does not choose food." Although this is a thousand-year-old saying, there is still room for correction. No matter how hungry and thirsty you are, you cannot eat poison or snatch other people's life-saving soup to eat. Women today are indeed suffering from the same urgency as hunger and thirst, but in this urgency, they still cannot stumble blindly in confusion. Instead of having the courage to commit suicide, murder, and various meaningless self-destructive acts, why not use it to fight this society? As long as we can overcome the various restrictions in life and thought, we have a life that is just as important as a man's. It is only because the status of the entire society in the world is low that we women have today's new oppression and new bondage; we must fight for women's equal status in society and the equal status of society in the world. Merely destroying ourselves is not the right way.

Do not put personal comfort, love, and vanity first, but take the brightness of society as a prerequisite. Society does not need people to abandon themselves, but needs people to bravely struggle and sacrifice. Although the situation is urgent, we women must not admit defeat and fall into the path of destruction.

Love and Murder

— Zi Jiu

While the discussion of “Who killed Ruan Lingyu” still occupies much newspaper space, another piece of news about a love triangle murder case suddenly emerges. Various newspapers use headline-sized characters to show the seriousness and peculiarity of the matter. The protagonist of the tragic case, Liu Jinggui, a student at the Beiping North American Art School, was once in love with the athlete Dai Ming and had a marriage agreement. However, soon after, Dai Ming met Teng Shuang, a physical education teacher at Zhicheng Middle School, during the North China Games. Consequently, Dai Ming paid Liu Jinggui six hundred yuan to terminate the agreement and married Teng Shuang. From then on, Liu Jinggui harbored deep resentment and vowed revenge. Eventually, he shot and killed his rival in love, Teng Shuang, and became a prisoner himself. Murder is a path to death, and Liu Jinggui certainly understood this. This makes the social significance of murder and self-imprisonment no less serious than the question of "Who killed Ruan Lingyu," thus attracting much attention from various parties.

On the 20th of this month, the Morning Post published an article titled "Reflections on the Liu Jinggui Case" by Mr. Lin Gengbai. At the outset, he made the following statement about contemporary Chinese society:

"Modern Chinese society, filled with contradictory consciousness and ideologies, seems to have entered a divergent path in the past year or two. On the one hand, a new culture has not yet been established, while on the other hand, the old, declining culture is gradually raising its head. We deeply recognize that at this stage, China urgently needs to strive for the revival of national culture, but the revival of national culture should have two basic conditions: one is the completion of 'anti-feudal culture,' and the other is the establishment of 'anti-imperialist culture.' At the same time, it must be understood that feudal culture is not the spiritual foundation of our national culture, but rather it is a fatal wound that destroys the beautiful national culture... As for the invasion of imperialist culture, it seems everyone is very clear about it, but the cultural movement of these many years has not only failed to eliminate its influence but has instead propelled its wheels. This pathological overcorrection is exactly the opposite of the illusion of being infatuated with feudal culture, and unconsciously stands in opposition."

After making this analysis, Mr. Lin then raised the Liu Jinggui case, considering it a product of the struggle between the old and the new, and a social problem worthy of discussion. This analysis is correct, but Mr. Lin did not clearly point out why the old, declining culture is gradually raising its head, and why the invasion of imperialist culture remains the same. Not only remains the same, but according to Mr. Lin's observation, it is precisely "propelling its wheels"! Therefore, the social pathology of the Liu Jinggui murder case seems to only be a superficial explanation, without touching its root. Now, I would like to add to Mr. Lin's analysis, which may make the social pathology clearer.

Originally, the so-called "culture" is the superstructure of society, while the foundation of the lower layers of society is the economic organization. China's inherent economic organization has already disintegrated, and a new organization has not yet been established under the joint attack of internal and external troubles. In the process of being driven to a dead end, some people are nostalgic for the past, thinking that returning to the past may be a solution. Thus, returning to the past has become a new plan for the new China. The economic organization of the past created a society with feudal ideology. In the call for returning to the past, the feudal economic organization certainly cannot be revived in modern Chinese society, but feudal culture can be revived to poison the youth of modern China. On the other hand, the aggression of imperialists is intensifying day by day. Although there is talk of genuine friendship and high-sounding slogans, anyone with a discerning mind will realize the "tacit understanding" in it. We have no solutions in economics or politics now, so how can "anti-imperialist culture" be produced? Even if it can be produced, who would cherish it like Mr. Lin, who is so insightful? Therefore, "propelling its wheels" is an inevitable and natural phenomenon.

The foundation-filling economic organization has collapsed, and of course, it cannot produce a more "beautiful culture," "so in today's Chinese society, there are only remnants of the feudal social customs of the fifteenth and sixteenth centuries" (to borrow Mr. Lin's words). China is a semi-colony, and complete modern capitalism is of course impossible, "but the growth of the consciousness and emotions of capitalist society in the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries" (to use Mr. Lin's words again) is possible. In this current Chinese society, where old wounds have not healed and new poisons are added, what kind of young people are produced? Dai Ming and Liu Jinggui are the best representatives of the middle social class. Individualistic, selfish, and self-interested views of life dominate their entire consciousness. To satisfy their own private sorrows, they disregard the interests of others. At the same time, they are all short-sighted, unable to see society, unable to see the world, unable to see the future, unable to see the real enemy, only knowing what they want to do individually. Especially economically well-off young men, taking advantage of social advantages, pursue the opposite sex, changing affections from morning to night, which is their daily routine. Young women, because the feudal atmosphere still surrounds them, and feudal consciousness is still deeply rooted in their minds, and they have no real economic power in their hands, although they yearn for free love, in the end, they still regard marriage as a lifelong nursing home and regard men as lifelong backers. Therefore, the occurrence of changes in this nursing home and the seizure of the backer is a lifelong disaster, so how can they not be cautious and vigilant? Thus, the weak often cautiously defend against rivals in love. If they cannot win, they commit suicide, and if they cannot commit suicide, they end up depressed. The strong (although temporarily strong, are still equivalent to suicide and are still weak) often take adversarial offensive actions. Liu Jinggui's killing of Teng Shuang is an example. Dai Ming's romantic behavior and playing with women is precisely the consciousness and emotions of "capitalist society in the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries" that color him. Because only such a society can give him such freedom. Liu Jinggui's jealousy because of lost love, and his mutual slaughter with the same kind because of jealousy, are cultivated by "feudal habits of the fifteenth and sixteenth centuries" and "heroism" and "individualism" of the "eighteenth and nineteenth centuries". In feudal society, women are ashamed of being abandoned and have no real economic power. At the same time, heroism and individual thought make her only have herself. And if there is a conflict of interest with herself, she kills without hesitation. Even if she commits a crime, she doesn't care. Liu Jinggui, under the double attack of these poisons, finally became a murderer.

Therefore, although Liu Jinggui's murder and Dai Ming's playing with women are certainly their own fault, if these two young people were not born into this current society attacked by the new and old poisons, they would definitely not be like this. But now they have become criminals of society. This society, filled with evil air, poisons the young people with weak wills, making them criminals of society. Society poisons them and them. And the fallen young people have exacerbated the disorder of society. The two evolve in a cyclical manner.

Satisfying one's personal desires, venting personal habits, murder and suicide, if this continues, social order will become more chaotic and increasingly deepened.

Therefore, to make this society return to peace and tranquility, it is necessary to eliminate the new and old poisons that harm society. To eliminate these new and old poisons, as Mr. Lin Gengbai said, it is necessary to "complete the anti-feudal culture" and "establish the anti-imperialist culture."

Women's Issues Lecture Series

Section 2: Marriage and Family Forms in Primitive Times

— Jun Hui

According to historians, it has been about 25,000 years since humans emerged from the animal state to the present (the so-called origin of modern humans in history), but there are only four or five thousand years of recorded history. In this way, humans slowly evolved from the distant past into cultured people like today. In this long process of evolution, human economic, social, moral, and sexual relationships must also adapt to the evolutionary stages of human beings and have various different forms, just as black people and white people today have different male-female relationships and lifestyles.

Many shortsighted bourgeois scholars only see the male-female relationship since history began and believe that women's non-independence and subordination to men are determined by history. Since it was like this in the past, it must be like this in the future. At the same time, they believe that the family and marriage form of monogamy is natural and immutable. This view is either intentional deception or ignorant exposure.

We know that the status of women in society or the family is closely related to the stage of economic development. In other words, the position occupied by women in the stage of economic development, that is, the nature of the productive labor they bear, determines the status of women in society or the family. Family and marriage forms are also inseparable from the stage of economic development. For example, the family and marriage forms in the agricultural economic stage and the industrial economic stage are completely different.

Regarding the male-female relationship in primitive society, Bachofen's research is very interesting. In his book "Mother Right" (Droit-materna), he elaborates on the evolutionary process of human sexual relationships. The important points are as follows:

(1) In primitive humans, the sexual relationship was promiscuous.

(2) This type of sexual intercourse did not allow for the establishment of paternity. Children only knew their mother and did not know their father, thus giving rise to the matrilineal system, that is, the matriarchal system. All ancient peoples originated from this.

(3) As a result, women and motherhood became the only recognized relatives of posterity. The degree to which they enjoyed respect, according to Bachofen's imagination, reached the point where they had matriarchal rule.

(4) Later, it transitioned to monogamy, and women were exclusively at the disposal of men. (Refer to Cai Hesen's "History of Social Evolution")

After Bachofen, Morgan collected a lot of material on this aspect among various barbarian peoples, thus confirming the correctness of Bachofen's research. Moreover, he further systematically studied the family and marriage forms in primitive times. He divided the primitive marriage and family system into the following four types, and these four forms are properly adapted to the stage of social and economic development. Now, according to Morgan's opinion, a simple explanation is given for each form for the reader's reference.

(1) Consanguineous Marriage Family

Humans initially lived in groups, engaging in collective survival competition with poisonous snakes, fierce beasts, or foreign races. They all relied on acquiring natural objects to maintain a common life. Whether strong or weak, male or female, they could only live in this common group. Individuals had no possibility of surviving alone. Under this circumstance, on the one hand, in order to strengthen unity, and on the other hand, in order to reproduce the race, group marriage was practiced in the consanguineous group. That is, brothers and sisters naturally became a group of couples. In this group, there is a matriarch who is the master of this community. The so-called matriarchal clan originated from this.

(2) Punaluan Marriage Family Humans entered the early stage of the uncivilized era. Production tools were quite developed, and the cultivation of grains and the raising of livestock were invented. In this era, the productive labor of grains and livestock was borne by women, and men were engaged in war and hunting. Therefore, women occupied an important position in the economy. This is the economic foundation for the emergence of the matrilineal clan. Here, with the matrilineal system as the center, the inheritance of property was also limited to women. As for the marriage form, because humans entered the early stage of the uncivilized era, they experienced that consanguineous marriage was harmful to their racial reproduction. Therefore, they used the matrilineal system to divide bloodlines, and a group of brothers and a group of sisters who did not belong to the same mother made a group marriage. The so-called matriarchal era began from this.

(3) Pairing Marriage Family

This is a family formed by temporary monogamy. Humans reached the middle and late stages of the uncivilized era. Agriculture and animal husbandry were quite developed. The economic life of the matrilineal clan was very rich, and men could not inherit their mother's inheritance. Therefore, they could only join the wife's clan group to live. Men had no economic control and only performed the task of war for the wife's clan. At this time, although the marriage form was a monogamous union, its separation and reunion were very easy. This is the peak period of matriarchy.

(4) Polygynous Marriage Family

This is the family form that occurred after the matriarchal system was overturned and the patriarchal system was established. In this era, the technology of agriculture and animal husbandry developed, and the form of labor also changed, requiring a large amount of labor. Therefore, the prisoners captured by men from war were no longer killed but were used as slaves to make them work. In this way, production became more prosperous, and there were surplus things in addition to consumption. From then on, men used the preferential right of economic control to command slaves to overthrow the matriarchal system and establish the patriarchal system. The so-called patriarchal clan occurred from this. The head of the clan was a man. They plundered women from foreign races from war to be their wives and concubines, thus forming a polygamous family. The so-called plunder marriage was a product of this era.

From then on, not only did women become slaves of men, but with the occurrence of the private property system, differences in classes such as rich, poor, noble, and lowly also occurred between men. The primitive community of joint production and joint consumption has also forever become a historical relic!

The Life of Women in the Rural Areas of Western Shanghai

— Hua

In western Shanghai, outside the circle of roads built across the border, villages where families live together are scattered like chess pieces in the crisscrossing vegetable fields. Their main livelihoods are farming, doing petty business, pulling carts, and selling labor in factories.

Women, in addition to shouldering the burden of life like men, must also add the labor of cooking, washing clothes; taking care of children, making shoes, and mending torn clothes, which are needless to say.

Here, the support of a family's livelihood is actually not men, but women. In every couple, women always occupy an important role in production.

In farming couples, men spend most of their days leisurely going east and west; weeding, hoeing, and fertilizing are mostly women's duties. Letting older children roll around in garbage heaps, enduring all dangers, letting babies clinging to their breasts lie at home crying, they stay in the fields. When their backs are sore, they carry a full load of vegetables before they can come back; panting: "Oh, I'm exhausted!" They throw their headscarves aside, sit down, and the crying baby nestles in their arms. The little fellow tugs and pulls, crying because he's hungry. The mother, who hasn't even caught her breath yet, has to hurry to cook dinner. Before the sky is completely light, if the fields don't need them to do any work today, it is often the wife who carries vegetables to the street to sell. ——Generally, husbands are always more leisurely than wives.

Working men have their washing and cooking arranged by their mothers, wives, and daughters. If they are bachelors, cheap restaurants can solve their eating problems. What about women? They don't have such blessings! Not only do they still cook and wash their own clothes, but if they have children, they cannot shirk the responsibility of raising and caring for them; moreover, economically, the wages they earn cannot be handled as freely as men's. Their parents, brothers, or in-laws and husbands are very strict in their restrictions on them. They must hand over all their income to the head of the family: "How can I not hand it over? Expenses for gifts and the family's food and drink are all paid by him!" To make a piece of clothing, they still have to ask them for it, and they often suffer impolite rejections. They get up very early in the morning, and those whose factories are far away have to run three or five miles. Twelve hours of labor, plus the time spent running and eating, wastes fifteen or sixteen hours a day, but they can only get four or five jiao, or at most eight or nine jiao in pay; working the night shift is even more tiring. When they come back during the day, the children cry and shout, and it is difficult to steal a moment to sleep soundly after taking care of housework. Therefore, here, it is very common and not surprising for girls to flirt and sell their charm to try to earn extra money, and for women to throw their babies into the foundling home where mothers and children can never see each other again. The prosperity of capitalism, which squeezes their blood and sweat, means that in addition to the double burden of housekeeping and raising children, they must dedicate their working time to the factory; unbearable burdens wear them down. Whether in the factory or at home, they are treated as living machines. The women who bear the burden of their children's livelihood, the girls who are favored by the foreman and the nomor wan, are both docile and skilled. Women here almost all have these qualifications.

Women's abilities are strikingly active here! But in terms of status, it doesn't improve because of their strong and capable skills, and because they are the pillars of family livelihood; men still have supreme master authority, all social interactions and recreational enjoyment are mostly for men, and all heavy and tedious burdens are mostly for women.

The spring breeze tenderizes the fields that crisscross the thousands of acres, and it is busy farming season. Working in the lush green vegetable fields, their faces are burned red by the sun, their waists are bent low, agile and light, the edges of the fields are piled with discarded weeds, and the solidified soil is hoed loose. A soft wind teases the headscarves covering their heads. They are as beautiful as a group of butterflies playing in the flowers; majestic and wild like wild horses, they shuttle back and forth busily in the fields; giving people an impression of healthy, lively, and magnificent survivors.

However, the price of vegetables, which is lower year after year, means that their hard work is equal to waste, and there are many who have difficulty living. Often, they shout out their suffocating pain: "Life is bitter..." This unbearable heavy pressure is widely and deeply persecuting the farmers surrounding this prosperous city day by day.

When they are able to receive the clothes that students from schools solicit for washing, it is common to wash seventy or eighty pieces by hand in a day.

Whether it's calling out for business or pushing dung carts... all kinds of labor that are allowed by society, women are working without falling behind.

They are full of energy to create human happiness, but part of their vitality is deprived, and "heroes have no place to use their strength"; part of them exist for the sake of idle men and the burdens of the family; living like stray dogs and horses.——They can never obtain their own happiness in the happiness of mankind!

If their strong life energy had sufficient opportunities for development, would moving mountains and overturning seas be a difficult thing? Who says they can't overturn the subordinate status of women for thousands of years?

Diary of a Concubine

— Lulu

March 4th

Yesterday my luck was truly terrible. Just as I was about to win that hand, that cursed whore ruined it. I've been losing continuously these past few days.

The "Director" always says he hasn't been involved with her lately, but why bother arguing with him? What was that ring bought for yesterday? He said it was for the Second Miss's wedding, what a lie! The Second Miss isn't getting married until next autumn, why buy a ring so early? Besides, the Old Mistress doesn't even know about it.

He didn't come back until almost dawn again. Said he was busy with official business! Busy drinking and womanizing! Even that cursed whore can't find him. I wonder what new tricks he's up to.

March 6th

I misunderstood him the day before. According to Mrs. Zhao, they were indeed having a shareholder meeting at the Yangzi Company that day, and no women attended. They just played a few rounds of mahjong among themselves. Besides, he even won money back, so maybe it's true.

Yesterday afternoon, he smoked too much opium, and he hasn't been sleeping well for two nights. If he wants to sleep well, I won't have peace! There's nothing I can do, just like he often tells me: "If you start spending money, I won't have peace." It's no wonder, the doctor said I'm sick, so I'm especially averse to that kind of thing. But if he goes to that cursed whore, I'm really unhappy. What can I do? What do men spend money on women for? I can only...! Alas, Mother used to say: "A blessed woman is one who can please a man."

March 7th

Today is the anniversary of the Second Miss's mother's death, and the Old Mistress has been making a fuss about holding a vegetarian feast since early this morning. What's the point of making such a fuss? Even if you're more particular, the person is still dead. The "Director" plays around outside every day, and she doesn't even try to control him, always telling people that concubines are bought with money and aren't worth anything. Actually, she used to say the same thing about her daughter-in-law: "Men can always find women easily as long as they have money." Now she's respecting the dead to mock the living. You should know that you're a woman too! Really, what's the difference between marrying and buying? Sleeping with a man using his money is the same thing!

He came back very early this afternoon and stayed in my room the whole time. He probably encountered some unpleasant opponents outside, so he's being so nice to me. He even said he'll take me to the company to buy things tomorrow. But why did he suddenly say I'm too thin and not as attractive as Mrs. Gu Yuanru's chest? I know he's joking with me, but...

March 8th

Mrs. Gu Yuanru ran over early this morning, crying and sobbing, which really scared me. I was still dreaming and jumped out of bed. It turned out she had another fight with Mr. Gu and wanted a divorce. This is almost the same as our Fifth Mistress at home, who wants a divorce at least nine times a year. But before the divorce papers are even drawn up, they're hugging and kissing again. Sure enough, I had just washed my face this morning and hadn't even dried Mrs. Gu's tears when her husband came to pick her up. I heard that another car went to the Jai Alai court that night.

Later, I heard that they were arguing this time because Gu Yuanru wanted to marry another woman. I think if it's true, I should advise Mrs. Gu not to mention the word "divorce." In this kind of world, if a man wants to remarry, it's too easy for him if the woman initiates the divorce. Isn't it good for him if you remove the obstacle? So it's best not to leave, and move out instead, with the man paying for daily expenses.

I think I must visit the Gu's tomorrow afternoon to see what's going on.

March 12th

The Gu's affairs have made me dizzy these past few days. I absolutely do not approve of Mrs. Gu divorcing. Miss Lian is such a strange person. Whenever she encounters such situations, she always advises the woman to divorce. She always says that it's better not to have such a man than to let him mess around. It's better to be poor and live alone.

That's well said, and I often think that way when I'm very angry with those cursed whores. And I even really left once. For example, the time I had that fight with the "Director" the year before last, the nun Master Miao was so eager to persuade me to go to her convent. When I first went, she personally went to the kitchen to prepare vegetarian dishes every day, and she brought her little apprentice, Long Yu, to keep me company. She said, "It's better to become a nun. Involvement in the secular world always brings worries. Besides, to be honest, don't get angry, Madam, but you're almost thirty this year, and your 'Director' has always loved being a playboy and has a lot of money. He might marry one or two at any time. Then your position as wife will still be taken away, won't it? Oh?"

She also said to me, "As long as you sincerely believe in Buddha and have so much money in your own hands, you can live here peacefully in this convent. When I die, everything will be yours."

At that time, I really believed Master Miao's words. But I hadn't even lived there for three months when almost all my things were pawned, and there was no news from the "Director." Then, before Master Miao could even speak, the whole convent's attitude towards me changed. Later, if the "Director" hadn't listened to Secretary Li's persuasion, had a change of heart, and taken me back, I don't know what my fate would have been.

March 13th

I didn't finish writing yesterday's diary because Miss Lian came. As soon as she came, she started talking about Mrs. Gu's affairs. And how scary! It was yesterday afternoon, just as we finished watching the first movie, that she swallowed opium paste! Later, it was Miss Lian's sister-in-law, Miss Gu the Third, who discovered it first! She called Director Wang, saying that her aunt had taken poison, and Director Wang sent an ambulance to take her to the hospital.

When Miss Lian talked about this matter, she still advocated divorce. I took the opportunity to tell her about my experience of entering the convent the year before last. She said that the idea of entering the convent was wrong in the first place. Nuns always cheat people out of their money. Who really wants to help people wholeheartedly? I said that the matter of divorce is wrong in the first place. People in this world always oppress women. Where else can women turn if they don't rely on men! Miss Lian is not married now, and her father has such power. Who wouldn't want to hire a capable daughter? But if she gets married in the future, has children, and circumstances change, and her father is not like he is now, who will she turn to with her children in tow?

Miss Lian didn't say anything after hearing my words. I think she must be in love lately, otherwise why would her emotions change so strangely? When she's happy, she talks so much, and when she's depressed, she doesn't say a word.

March 21st

The Gu's crisis is over. Yesterday, the couple went out shopping hand in hand again, and they even invited us to eat at the Red Plum Restaurant in the evening. It seems that the Red Plum Restaurant specializes in reconciling husbands and wives. The last time our Fifth Mistress and her husband had a fight, the "Director" ended up inviting them to eat at the Red Plum Restaurant and they reconciled.

It's never worthwhile for the woman to take the initiative when a couple argues. People always say that women are petty and love to argue, and they're easily appeased with money. From now on, I will always try my best to avoid arguing. (To be continued)

*Shen Bao* Local Supplement, Amateur Weekly

Amateur Chats

The Philosophy of "Busy"

— Ms. Huang Ying

Humans are different from pigs. After pigs have eaten their fill, they can sleep in their pen all day without doing anything. But humans can't just eat and sleep without doing anything. A social person who lives in time and space has their energy consumed by changes in space and the progress of time. Due to the constant changes in space and the constant progress of time, human life is also constantly changing and progressing. Therefore, human energy is also constantly being consumed. But this is inevitable. Every second and minute that time progresses, human energy must be consumed accordingly. Because only when humans constantly consume their energy can history progress forward due to human impetus. Therefore, a living social person cannot be like a dead, static object, rigidly occupying a certain space and letting time fly by in vain. They must be active, work, and do things. On the one hand, they are consuming their energy and time. At the same time, on the other hand, they are continuing to live and pursuing the joys of life. If a normal, living person has nothing to do every day after eating, doesn't know how to consume their energy, and just stares blankly as time progresses, then I believe they will be very distressed, even unable to live. We see that those wealthy old masters and mistresses are not able to and don't want to do anything proper, right? But precisely because they have nothing proper to do, they have to desperately engage in those boring activities, such as dancing, gambling, chasing after the opposite sex, playing with dogs and cats, etc., to consume their energy. If you were to tell these wealthy and therefore idle old masters and mistresses not to study equations (play mahjong), not to go to the Jai Alai court and dance halls, not to keep a very human-like dog, and not to pursue sexual stimulation, think about it, where would their energy be consumed? How painful would their spirit be? Furthermore, look at the so-called petty bourgeoisie, aren't there many gentlemen who are called "busy doing nothing"? Actually, it's precisely because they have nothing specific to do, their lives have no center, their spirits have no place to rest, that they have to run around on the streets every day, find friends, brag emptily, and put on a busy-as-hell appearance.

Yes, a living social person is different from a pig that eats its fill and does nothing. They must work and be active in order to consume their energy. But there are many things in the world. Working, doing business, teaching, writing articles are work and things. Gambling, dancing, smoking opium, broadly speaking, are also work and things. Revolution or becoming a traitor can still be said to be work and things. Among these things, which are proper? What should we do in our own life process? Mr. Liang Qichao, in his famous essay "What is the Purpose of Life?", questioned all kinds of people about why they are busy and then said: "Busyness is the duty of life. Look at the great figures of ancient and modern times, both Chinese and foreign, such as Yu the Great, Mozi, Sakyamuni, and some supervising figures, as well as other saints, sages, heroes, and outstanding figures. Which of them would steal leisure for themselves? Which of them were not too busy to warm their seats, unable to be silent, running around in haste, and doing so their entire lives? If one hates busyness and seeks leisure, wouldn't they become mere clothes racks and food sacks? As for talking about hating the world, only the dictionary of a person without ambition has these two words. The sages of ancient times never said such a thing. Please do not misunderstand. What I am saying is to tell you to be busy all day long, busy all year round, but always busy towards a goal. What have you been busy with in the past and present? What is the purpose? Not only do I not know, I'm afraid even you yourself don't know. Not only do you yourself not know, I'm afraid you have never even thought about it since you were born. Alas! Life is impermanent, a human body is hard to obtain. Several decades of cold and heat pass in the blink of an eye. Today's youth, how long will it be before they suddenly become strong and sturdy, suddenly decline and become old, suddenly die unexpectedly, confused and muddled, covered head to toe, wrapped in pus and blood, spending this life like this, isn't it pitiable! Isn't it regrettable! What's more, this kind of purposeless life is bound to be entangled with all kinds of worries and troubles. How can one pass the long night! I advise you to seek the root and investigate the bottom, and come up with a topic, which is to tell you to seek light in the darkness, to teach you to find a place to settle down and establish your life." "Busyness is the duty of life," but we must be busy with a purpose and not waste our energy casually. What is the purpose? It should be to "seek light in the darkness." - This is truly worthy of being the words of a pioneer and visionary! The question of what we should be busy with in the life process and what we should do also has a clear answer in this correct statement: that is, we should be busy seeking light in the darkness, and do things that seek light in the darkness.

We have already stated above that the progress of history depends on the driving force of humanity. If the continuous impetus of humanity to advance history is that humanity is increasingly moving from darkness to light, then the so-called "seeking light in the darkness" in concrete terms is pushing history forward. Therefore, we can say this: "Busyness is the duty of life." People must do things, and promoting the progress of history is the highest principle of our being "busy" with doing things. Under this principle, pursuing low-level entertainment is of course something we should not do. Running around on the streets, bragging, and the so-called "busy doing nothing" are also things that we should consider boring and despise. In our social life, we must contribute our energy to social movements that promote the progress of history and strive to do work that is beneficial to social development. Only in this way can we avoid wasting our energy, and only in this way can we fulfill our "duty of life."

Of course, saying this does not mean that all young students should leave school and all workers and shop clerks should leave their factories and shops... to participate in social movements that promote the progress of history. No. The so-called social movements that promote the progress of history do not unfold in the vastness of space, but arise and develop among the general populace. Therefore, the workplace where people promote the progress of history is in general society and also in their professional lives.

Since the progress of history depends on the driving force of humanity, the size of an individual's contribution to human society is directly proportional to the amount of force they add to promoting the progress of history. But in order for a person to possess a great power to promote the progress of history, they must have the ability to recognize the direction of historical progress and have the observational power to know how the power to promote historical progress works. At the same time, this kind of ability and observational power do not come from talent, but are formed in the life experiences of acquired nature. Therefore, if a person wants to increase their power to promote the progress of history, they must often go among the people to investigate the general actual social situation, and often read newspapers, news, and general theoretical and practical books in order to enrich their knowledge and increase their ability to recognize the objective world.

Life

Form Creator

— Qian Ping

In the former warlord era, the offices I stayed in could be listed at great length: county government, tax bureau, police department. However, my work was always the same: "form creator." This wasn't because I liked doing this work, nor because my superiors particularly favored me. It was simply because I was too junior to get any more relaxing position!

The forms I created were mostly about expense reimbursements. No matter what kind of organization it was, it always came down to income and expenses and official travel expenses. It seemed very simple, but when you actually did it, you found it extremely troublesome. On the one hand, your penmanship had to be fast and good, and you had to be proficient with the abacus. If your writing was a little sloppy or your calculations were a little off, that was a big problem. If your own superior discovered it, it wasn't too serious, at most you'd get a mark or a pay cut. But if it was rejected and returned by the higher-ups, even your superior would be reprimanded. All superiors in the world value their reputation and hope to be promoted several levels. For a form creator who ruins their "

Page 18

official reputation" and "official luck," it's really not easy to let them off lightly! Originally, the bottom line of the so-called "four-column ledger" for the income and expenditure of expenses and the salaries of the staff was provided by the accounting department. But they were either relatives or old friends of the superior, and instead ordered us to do their own duties for them. This way, we had two jobs at once, which not only increased the workload but also meant bearing a lot of responsibility!

No matter what kind of organization it was, there was always a definite regulation for official expenses. If you actually spent and reported what you spent, then handling the forms would just be a matter of recording the information. However, in the former warlord era, the problem wasn't that simple. There were even more hidden reasons! Although there were definite regulations for official expenses, spending more meant the superior was responsible, and spending less meant the remainder had to be returned. The superior wasn't a fool, of course they wouldn't spend more and report less. Conversely, they would only spend less and report more. The so-called "reporting more" meant exactly meeting the regulations.

In short, the actual expenditure was minimized by the superior, and the reimbursement form had to be filled out by us form creators so that nothing was left. Doing this tricky work wouldn't be too difficult if we just used our brains to imagine a few numbers and fill them in appropriately under the expense items on the form. However, higher-level organizations were very particular about evidence, meaning that if there was a pen on the reimbursement form, you had to attach an invoice from the stationery store. Heavens, where were we going to find that invoice? The entire reimbursement figure was fabricated, where were we going to find so much evidence? As a result, we form creators had to open stationery stores, rice shops, and coal factories in our minds... take good store names appropriately, go to a seal-carving shop to carve seals, and then ask someone to write out the invoices. Only then was the work considered complete. On the surface, it may not seem difficult, but to fabricate several store names and the value of goods out of thin air, you had to investigate and be familiar with the local situation at least a little to avoid any flaws!

It was even more difficult on the travel expense side. The superior was originally at home and didn't send anyone on a business trip, but every month they still had to reimburse dozens or hundreds of yuan in travel expenses. For example, inspecting river works cost one hundred yuan, investigating murder cases cost fifty yuan... The higher-ups also wanted definite evidence, and a detailed receipt for what hotel you stayed in and what dishes you ate. This way, we had to especially study the geography of that place: how far a certain town was from a certain city, how many hotels there were, and what restaurants there were. Other local customs and practices also needed some investigation. After all the prerequisites were arranged, our bodies as form creators were sitting in the office, but our minds were on a business trip dozens or hundreds of miles away. This wasn't too bad, but what made my head hurt the most was the collection of dish names and the estimation of values, because there were several travel expense reimbursements every month, and each business trip had to be assumed to last three or five days. In order to make the fakes look believable, the dish names were best not to be the same for each meal, and each dish had to be suitable for the local environment. For example, twice-cooked pork is a common dish in Sichuan, but it couldn't be filled in on the reimbursement form of a certain organization in the north. Western food in big cities couldn't appear in small restaurants in towns... This way, we couldn't get a moment of leisure outside the office: on the one hand, we had to investigate the names of dishes, and at the same time, we had to pay attention to their normal values. We couldn't ask the local pretty people about this stupid thing, and we couldn't ask the coolies (they had never been to restaurants at all). We mostly ran to nearby big and small restaurants, recorded the menu, or asked the chefs. After this problem was solved, we slept in bed and carefully considered: in the morning, we should eat a plate of braised pork tripe, and at night, we needed a pot of Huadiao wine and two plates of cold dishes. The next day, the third day, we had to change to a different pattern...!

Therefore, my work in the office was nominally form creation, but in reality, I also had to be a clerk, a merchant, a chef... I couldn't even have a pleasant bowel movement during the day, and I couldn't close my eyes as soon as I got into bed at night. The work was so troublesome, but my salary was at most twenty-four yuan. Although I helped others earn a lot of money, I never received a one or two yuan subsidy. - In fact, I never had such hope at all. I would be lucky if I could keep my job a little longer. But what's strange is that even this small wish often became a fantasy!

Training and Cultivation

The Way of "Employing People"

— Heng Yi

The same talent, employed by two different people, because of different methods of use, often leads to different results. How to make people obey, make them accept your ideas, concentrate their efforts, even give their lives, and be willing to work hard, is a question that a businessperson should study.

However, people are living things, not as easy to control as machines. The manipulation of people requires "subtlety," and "natural compliance." Kongming's treatment of Meng Huo, capturing him seven times and releasing him seven times, was nothing more than the influence of virtue. That's why I say that only an unintelligent leader would abandon the fundamental and pursue the superficial, failing to make people submit from the root, and instead use the stupid method of "threats" and "inducements" to forcibly win people over.

Experienced businesspersons can generally feel that those who are willing to go through fire and water and give their lives are definitely not because they are paid more during peacetime.

A businessperson who can employ people and knows how to employ people has taken the first step towards the success of their business. Otherwise, no matter how grand your ambitions are, if you only have people tearing down pillars and no green leaves to set you off, then success or failure has already been decided from the beginning. Now let's discuss "how to employ people."

First, you should "deeply understand human nature." At the beginning of employing a person, you must first examine that person's humanity. If this person has admirable qualities, and you want to bring them into your service, then you should give them an attitude of trust in all respects." This is what is called having a discerning eye. You cannot erase their strengths just because they come from a humble background. Everyone has their noble impulses. If they can gain your trust, they will naturally strive to exert their abilities in order to repay your kindness in the future.

The so-called "trust" is definitely not the so-called "laissez-faire." Therefore, those who are good at employing people have an attitude of trust on the surface, but they may still secretly monitor or restrain them. Linking trust and restraint together may seem contradictory on the surface, but in fact, when leading the masses, they are indeed not mutually exclusive and have a synergistic effect.

Second, you must rely on the influence of your personality. I often say that the power of personality to influence people is the greatest. It is enough to make people weep and enough to make people tremble. Just as the ancients said: "Sincerity can move even metal and stone."

If you ask where personality comes from, simply put, personality originates from human nature. Human nature is condensed and expressed in form, and only then does it become a person's personality. A person's personality can never be discovered from just one aspect, nor can it be judged solely on one aspect of their character, and considered a complete expression of their personality.

The ideal personality should first be able to control themselves. Emotions should be governed by reason. The world is a big arena, unpredictable. If you are not an extraordinary person, you cannot respond to extraordinary changes. When Mr. Sun Yat-sen was besieged in Guangzhou, the sound of gunfire was heard outside, but he remained calm as usual. This self-control, which restrains emotions and power, as expressed in his personality, was enough to make his followers admire the greatness of his personality and gain the allegiance of most people. Second, they can be selfless. Third, they can be non-envious. Fourth, they have peaceful integrity. Fifth, they have a cooperative spirit. Sixth, they are not jealous. Seventh, they have a clean example. Therefore, the so-called ideal personality is actually a person's natural prestige.

Therefore, in the way of employing people, one must first have the talent of a leader.

Scientific Business Talk

A Grand View of the Universe

— Compiled by Luo Lie

When speaking of the total expanse of cosmic space, even scientists cannot provide a concrete ultimate limit. They can only say that because the existence of matter is infinite, the vastness of the universe is also infinite. Although modern science is very advanced, the portion of cosmic space that it can observe is still very limited, at most only knowing a tiny corner of the universe. However, even this small corner of the finite space that is currently known is so grand and astonishing that merely talking about it can be shocking!

If you stand a mile away from a person who is four or five feet tall, that person will become a black dot, almost impossible to see. This means that a mile is not a short distance; it can shrink a four- or five-foot-tall person into a black dot, so it can be considered a fairly large distance in our direct visual perception. But if you ask how big the Earth is, then its diameter alone is about 7,920 miles. As for its circumference, each degree of latitude is about 69 miles, so multiplying that by 360 degrees gives a circumference of about 24,800 miles. The Earth's mass is 6,000,000,000,000,000,000,000 tons, which is sixty trillion trillion tons. In this way, the Earth can be considered a large mud ball suspended in the sky. However, considering just the eight major planets of the solar system, the Earth's volume is 1,300 times smaller than Jupiter's, its diameter is 11 or 12 times smaller than Jupiter's, more than 9 times smaller than Saturn's, more than 4 times smaller than Uranus's, and about 5 times smaller than Neptune's. As for the Earth compared to the Sun, it is even much smaller. The Sun's diameter is 866,400 miles, about 109 times larger than the Earth's, its volume is about 1.3 million times greater than the Earth's, and its weight is 332,000 times heavier than the Earth's. So, it would take almost a million or more Earths to make a single Sun.

The above only discusses the size of the Sun and planets. If we consider the space occupied by the solar system, Mercury, the closest planet to the Sun, is 36 million miles away, the Earth is 93 million miles away from the Sun, and Neptune is 2,797.16 million miles away from the Sun. So, if we consider only the Earth, with its 93 million miles distance from the Sun as the radius and the Sun as the center, drawing a circle (the Earth's orbit around the Sun is an ellipse, not a perfect circle), then the diameter of this circle would be 186 million miles. The Earth travels this circle at an orbital speed of 18 miles per second, taking a year, or about 31,536,000 seconds. Thus, this circle is about 567.64 million miles long. Considering the even more distant Neptune, the orbit it draws around the Sun has a diameter of 5,943.2 million miles, so the size of the space occupied by the solar system is imaginable. In this space, calculating with light traveling at 180,000 miles per second, it takes just over eight minutes for light to travel from the Sun to the Earth, and then just over four hours and thirty-six minutes to reach Neptune. If light were shot from one end of Earth's orbit to the other, it would take sixteen or seventeen minutes to arrive, and from one end of Neptune's orbit to the other, it would take more than nine hours. If a train traveling at 42 miles per hour were to travel from Earth to the Sun, it would take over 254 years to reach the Sun; and to reach the opposite end of the Earth's orbit, it would take over 500 years. If a cannonball with maximum speed were fired from Neptune, it would take 250 years to reach the center of the Sun, and 500 years to reach the opposite point of Neptune's orbit.

Are the Sun and the solar system considered large then? No, no. The Sun is a giant compared to Earth, but compared to other giant stars, it becomes a dwarf. The space occupied by the solar system is tiny compared to other clusters and nebulae. If we consider the size of the Sun as one unit, then the A star in Lyra is 2.4 times larger; the Y star in Scorpio is 3.2 times larger; the B star in Centaurus is 11 times larger; the A star in Auriga is 12 times larger; the A star in Bootes is 30 times larger; the A star in Taurus is 60 times larger; the B star in Pegasus is 170 times larger; the A star in Orion is 290 times larger; the O star in Hydra is 300 times larger; the A star in Hercules is 400 times larger; the A star in Scorpio is 480 times larger; and one of the brightest variable stars among the two shoulder stars of Orion would require 5,000 times the volume of the Sun to create it. As for stars with a diameter of over one million miles, there are quite a few, and the diameter of a variable star can even reach 300 million miles; the Earth's orbit around the Sun could almost be included within its circumference.

Astronomers divide the stars in the sky into regions for study, each region named after a principal star, becoming a constellation. Currently, there are 68 recognized constellations, and of course, more are still being discovered. Each constellation contains a large number of stars, ranging from thousands or tens of thousands to tens of millions. It is said that the spiral nebula in the Virgo constellation contains millions or even tens of trillions of stars. To calculate the spatial area of various star clusters, nebulae, and their distances in celestial bodies, miles are no longer a suitable unit, and light-years must be used. A light-year is the distance that light travels in a year at a speed of 185,000 miles per second. As we mentioned earlier, the diameter of the solar system's area, if light travels through it, would only take nine months. However, the nearest star outside the solar system, Alpha Centauri, is 25 trillion miles away, requiring 4.4 light-years to reach Earth. Sirius is 50 trillion miles away, or about 9 light-years. Some very distant spiral nebulae are 10 million light-years away because they are 60,000,000,000,000,000,000,000 miles away from our Earth. Not only that, there are even more distant objects in the sky; their light was emitted 100 million years ago, and only now reaches the eyes of astronomers. This means that astronomy can now observe a spatial distance of 100 million light-years.

Many of the fixed stars in the sky form their own solar systems. The densest place they inhabit is reflected in the sky as the Milky Way, which is 50,000 light-years wide in diameter and 3,000 to 4,000 light-years thick. The starlight from the farthest star on the edge of the Milky Way takes 50,000 years to reach the Earth. Like the aforementioned spiral nebula, its diameter is also 50,000 light-years, but it is only one of the most prominent nebulae in the island universes. In fact, in the visible universe, there are at least 100,000 nebulae. As for the fixed stars in the universe, current scientific estimates are at least 30

Page 19

trillion. From this perspective, in the discovered 100 million light-year universe, there are about 30 trillion fixed stars, and the island universes, where fixed stars are densely packed, have a domain as large as 50,000 light-years. Beyond that, there is the even more distant and sparse sky, which has not yet been explored by modern science and technology. So, in such a great and splendid sea of the universe, humans, compared to them, are probably as small as an electron compared to a ball, which is so amazing!

Art World

The Objectivity of Art

— Compiled by Yin Tan

I recently read a work by Ikkoku Kagaku, in which he discussed the difference between art and science, saying that science is objective, while art is subjective. The reason he holds is very simple, because the essence of science is to explain objective facts and laws, which is based on public recognition and universal agreement, and does not differ according to individual subjective feelings and opinions; moreover, facts and laws cannot be selectively chosen and tailored by individuals subjectively, so it is objective. Art is different. Art is about expressing the author's personal feelings, and personal feelings not only vary from person to person but also change all the time. Although art also uses objective things as objects of description, this is arbitrarily chosen by the artist themselves, freely combined and tailored according to their own viewpoints. The author personally organizes it from their own point of view, which they deem beautiful, and the viewer also judges it from their own point of view of beauty and feelings. Therefore, the author cannot simply describe objective facts little by little to create a work of art, and the viewer must also feel that it is beautiful in order to find it beautiful. These are all subjective.

Such a view of art is not only idealistic, but also too superficial and not profound enough in its understanding of art itself. Yes, any artificial product, if viewed from the perspective that it cannot be separated from human effort and the thinking of the brain, has some subjective color, especially all products of intelligence. However, this interaction between subjective and objective only has a parallel form when viewed from the most recent link in the active process of mental production. If we go a step further and ask about the ultimate source of these two opposing things, then objective facts always exist independently in the objective world, and the emergence of subjective thinking also originates from the objective. In this way, there is no independent and self-sufficient subjectivity. If we can understand the relationship between thinking and reality in this way, then the statement that art is subjective and science is objective is incorrect. It is only accurate and truthful to say that art and science are both objective.

For example, if science is about explaining objective facts and laws, then isn't art also based on objective reality? All great works of art must embody a deep objective background in order to become art and express its greatness, and to capture the audience's psychology and move their emotions. Any work without real significance will not have this effect. Idealistic artists and critics believe that a work of art, because it is something that ordinary people have not sensed, and the more it arouses the audience's interest and surprise, the more it is the author's personal spirit that moves people. In fact, the most moving works of art are still those that best depict the things inside reality. In other words, it is either able to highlight the special significance of facts from ordinary facts that ordinary people do not pay attention to, or because it sees certain essences of reality better than ordinary people. However, the so-called facts with special significance and certain essences cannot exist apart from reality. Great artists are able to use extraordinary means to dig out these hidden things to capture the audience's observation, which is precisely where the best depiction of reality lies. Naturally, there are often different societies, resulting in works that embody different realities, and audiences who have different observations of those works, and therefore cannot gain universal support. But to become a great and popular work, it must at least embody the reality of the life of the society to which it belongs in order to be possible. From this point of view, art, like science, is based on reality.

Secondly, it is also incorrect to say that science does not need to be tailored and matched to facts, while art needs to be tailored and matched by the writer's ingenuity. There is also tailoring and matching of facts in scientific research. Because when we study science to formulate laws, we must compare and match many messy phenomena, eliminate some external phenomena that are irrelevant to the topic, and examine which are similar in appearance but not in reality, or which are different on the outside but the same inside. What is tailoring and matching? As for the tailoring and matching of works of art, it is not entirely based on the author's free will; he must also follow objective laws to carry out his work in order to succeed. These objective laws are the laws of nature and society. For example, an artist, when filling in colors in the various combinations of his painting, must match them according to the natural and realistic scenery of the painting. He cannot just paint a pile of ink on a bouquet of flowers, because this does not conform to the beauty of nature. For example, a novel or movie cannot depict a beggar wearing a suit and leather shoes and taking a car to beg for food, because this also does not conform to the laws of social life. In this way, we can clearly see that the artist's work and ingenuity are the same as those of a scientist; they must select materials and choose and match raw materials according to objective laws in order to carry out his organizational and descriptive work.

True, art is about expressing the author's personal feelings, but only idealists believe that the author's personal feelings are personal, innate, self-sufficient, and have nothing to do with the objective. In fact, personal feelings are reflected and cultivated by society. The greater the artist, the more his feelings embody the feelings of society. Society must have coercion, and then there will be feelings of anger and resistance. The more the author's feelings can represent this kind of emotion, the more powerful the work will be to express the feelings of the author and society. The upper class of society must have a pleasant and leisurely life and happy feelings, and the author can create comedy works that represent certain lives. A madman who cannot embody social emotions, although he expresses his power without scruples, cannot be used as the content of any artistic activity. Not only are the personal feelings expressed in great works objective and social, but the feelings of the audience are also social. Works that are completely unrelated to their social public life and social psychology cannot capture their emotions, and they cannot express the same emotions to adapt to, appreciate, and welcome such works. In short, great art is a realistic and objective reflection, just like science. The science of art cannot be separated from reality, and cannot fail to embody reality. Art is also science. The more it embodies reality and organizes and studies art according to scientific methods, the more scientific the art is.

A Tour of the Shanghai Theater Opera Training Institute

— Compiled by Li Mei

Because I have always loved drama, in the past, as long as there was a good film, I couldn't escape seeing it no matter what. Especially for spoken drama, I have an unspeakable feeling; no matter what kind of theater troupe performs, I always go to admire it with enthusiasm.

Since the May Fourth Movement, the history of China's cultural movement has had commendable achievements, especially in spoken drama and literary creation, which have made great progress, although general art is also evolving in the same way.

However, due to the limitations of time and talent, drama alone has not been able to fully develop. In Europe, the popular and very common opera has remained rarely seen in our theater scene. People are just waiting for it with anticipation.

Recently, newspapers have been constantly publishing news about the Shanghai Theater Opera Training Institute. As of today, they have been in class for almost a week.

The emergence of this brand-new thing first attracted my attention and curiosity; and when I learned that only twenty people were admitted out of hundreds of applicants, it aroused my interest in visiting.

One morning, I hailed a rickshaw and happily went to this training institute. As soon as I walked in, they were in class, and their director, Mr. Chen Dabeui, came out to greet me. Under Mr. Chen's enthusiastic reception, I took a small tour. The impression their training institute gave me was very deep.

Twenty Healthy and Beautiful Children

When I first arrived at the training institute, I saw their classroom from outside the window. Twenty people, the women in front and the men in the back, sat in their seats with extreme solemnity and neatness, quietly listening to the instructor's lecture. So silent, no one coughed or said a word. I have spent more than ten years in school and have never seen such good order. So spirited, it is even more rare. I firmly believe that these lovely children are all very healthy. In my expectations, this training institute must be as romantic as ordinary theater troupes, but the facts proved that my speculation was completely wrong.

Their Equipment

It is a foreign-style house that is not small, located on Route Dollfus in the French Concession, diagonally opposite the French Park. As soon as you enter the door, mainly, you know that it is quiet and clean. Not only is it not similar to any theater troupe, it even surpasses the best schools—in cleanliness and order. In addition, in terms of equipment, although this training institute was established not long ago, it is not simple. Inside, there is a small library; they have painstakingly collected all the Chinese translations of world-famous plays, as well as things like principles, ideologies, and historical facts. There are also the latest equipment and facilities for music, dance, and expression.

Exceeded the Original Plan and Ideal

Initially, they planned to enroll a group of students with a secondary school education and gradually impart some knowledge and skills of opera to them. As a result of the enrollment, they were all highly educated, so they had to raise the original plan. This has further increased the interest of the instructors, who are lecturing with energy, hoping that the students will accept knowledge as if they were receiving an injection. After careful inquiry, I realized that each of their professors is a talent with specialized skills and rich experience, especially Mr. Wu Xiaobang. I secretly watched him teach dance, jumping up and down on the table, just like the Monkey King making a big disturbance in the Heavenly Palace.

Living in a Tense and Hard Paradise

This is what I heard from a student. He said: "We came here with determination. We are willing to dedicate our personal lives and souls to the cause of theatrical movement. We are very tough now, and maybe we will be even tougher in the future? But we will always overcome these difficulties with the greatest determination. We have nearly twenty subjects, and we have to take eight hours of classes every day. We don't have much time for rest and entertainment: because when we rest, everyone is doing homework, and entertainment has almost become our work, and work is our only entertainment. Our leg bones ache every day, and we can't go out until Sunday, but all this doesn't make us feel restricted. We dare to be confident: at least in our hearts, our classmates have put the heavy burden of the theatrical movement on their shoulders. ..."

My and Our Hope

The result of the tour was more satisfactory than I expected. I really didn't expect that there would be such a model in the theater troupe. Romance, laziness, and quarrels are absolutely not allowed in this training institute; it has all the characteristics of ordinary theater troupes: perseverance, hard work, and unity. Moreover, those twenty children are healthy, lively, brave, and loyal. The equipment is so complete: the professors are also very familiar; under such circumstances, we are wishing it future success.

Here, we silently pray for the success of the opera movement!

Miscellany

Night of Fishing

— You Ren

I love the countryside, especially living in the countryside; because there are unforgettable mountain peaks, water edges, verdant pine forests, and tranquil fields that can make me feel happy everywhere. Even the simple and robust song of the farmers, "When the sun rises, we go out to work; when the sun sets, we come back to rest," sounds more beautiful to me than whatever "Little Baby, Go to Sleep" is broadcast by the city's radio station. Even if I live in the countryside forever, I won't say things like "annoying" or "boring" as I would in the city. Country life makes me comfortable everywhere; especially fishing, which is a peculiar habit of mine. Every time I go fishing, it always makes me linger and forget to return.

It was an autumn evening. The rain had just cleared, and my cousin and I stood on a high earthen embankment, admiring the ever-changing white clouds and the jade-like bright moon. At this time, the herdboy's song of returning home after the rain, together with several fishermen's songs sent from afar, rang crisply and gracefully throughout the universe of nature, making me feel an unparalleled sense of beauty. My soul, unable to resist the lure of the songs, sang fishing songs as well. I wanted to go fishing, so I clung to my cousin, urging him to leave the high embankment and go home. Unable to withstand my pestering, my cousin had to agree. I was extremely happy! So we went home and quickly gathered our fishing gear—fish baskets, fish scoops, and raincoats and hats. After my cousin had folded the net, we went fishing together.

The earth was silent. Because of the rain, some farmers had already gone to sleep and rest; others were prevented by the rain from returning home. The old cow under the grass shed was sighing deeply; the little dog in front of the house was barking "Woof, woof" every now and then. There were few pedestrians on the road—almost no one. After walking a long way, we finally ran into Liu Er, a neighbor, carrying his farm tools home.

Walking further, we vaguely saw Xiao Shi driving two fat yellow oxen—they were pulling a "water cart," hurrying home. The road was muddy, and the cart was creaking. The oxen were panting, and Xiao Shi was still scolding them! The crack of a whip stirred the air on the earth from silence to excitement.

We met Xiao Shi, and mud splashed from under the cart.

"Just going home?" The enthusiastic question came out of my mouth again.

"Yes, because of the rain, I haven't finished working on the two acres of land!" He then said, "It's autumn now, and the river water is newly fallen. Where are you going fishing? You really have nothing to do! Aren't you afraid of getting sick from the cold water? Let's go home together!" Looking at the tools we were carrying, he guessed that we were going fishing; at the same time, he was concerned that the autumn rain had just fallen, and the night water was even colder, as if afraid that we would get sick from the rain, so he tried to stop us. But my cousin and I continued to move forward. Walking, walking, after turning a few bends, we stopped on a small bridge next to a clump of reeds. My cousin put the net down under the bridge and stood there silently. I spread out my raincoat and lay down on it. Quietly, as if expecting something.

The reeds by the bridge swayed in the night wind. The nearby sorghum stalks and soybean plants grew deeply, and although there was bright moonlight shining down, it still felt a bit gloomy. The frog drums in the fields were drumming particularly vigorously after the rain. At this time, I enjoyed the beautiful scenery before me, as if I had forgotten everything. Suddenly, I looked up and saw my cousin still standing there holding the net rod, motionless. The ripples on the water were illuminated by the moonlight, and the moon in the water also clearly showed a moving appearance. I had just recited the line "Water and sky, two moons, bright above and below." My cousin quickly said, "Don't sing, you'll scare the fish away!" At this time, all my attention turned to the net in my cousin's hand. The net was lifted, and water slid down from the net like silver threads. The ripples on the water surface spread outwards in circles. In the moonlight, they looked like ten thousand little white gold dragons swimming in a green glass bottle! After the water had dripped off, the net was empty! I was a little puzzled, why weren't there any fish in the net? Suddenly, I thought: Maybe we just arrived? Instantly, my heart returned to its previous calmness. The net was lifted, one net after another, but not even a shadow of a fish was seen!

"Are there no fish after the new rain?" I asked my cousin.

"Yes, wait a moment." My cousin was not in a hurry at all! He put the fishing net into the water again. The earth was even quieter, and the wind carried the night talks of two or three fishermen from nearby.

"Ah! Other people are also fishing! Perhaps the fish have been caught by them?" I asked my cousin again.

"No way, 'fish pass through a thousand nets'... Give me my tobacco pouch so I can smoke a pipe!" My cousin answered me while asking me to pass him the tobacco pouch. I thought that smoking could catch fish, so I hurriedly filled the pouch and handed it to my cousin. The net was lifted again, but still "empty"! The night wind increased in gusts, and I felt shivering because I was wearing thin clothes; but because I had desperately wanted to come, I had no choice but to endure it in silence. I hunched over, standing motionless and staring blankly at the net. Because I hadn't seen any fish for a long time, my eyes sometimes unconsciously wandered to the distant night scenery.

Continued on the fifth page

Page 20

Page 21

Finally, everything in the distance gradually became blurred. The moon was about to set! I was getting anxious when suddenly, my cousin said, "Fish are coming from afar, you can hear the sound of fish tails by the river." My cousin pulled back my infatuated eyes and turned them towards the net. Sure enough, I heard a gurgling sound in the water, and the fishing net was trembling greatly. Then, a fish was caught! "Quick!" It was my cousin's urgent voice. At this time, I panicked and forgot about the cold. I hurriedly grabbed the fish basket, didn't even take off my clothes, and jumped into the river with a splash.

"I told you not to rush, 'ten years without a market, when there is a market, eat for ten years.' Look at this fish, it weighs more than five catties!" My cousin shouted triumphantly. Looking at the big fish in his hand, the scales shone brightly in the moonlight, and I felt an indescribable joy in my heart. I just kept smiling. I didn't climb back onto the bridge, but just stood by the net. After that, the net was lifted, one net after another, and big fish, small fish, carp, crucian carp... one after another, we caught half a basket.

Before long, the Moon Sister went down the mountain, and two or three rooster crows came from the village. The dark shadows under the bridge gradually faded, and the clumps of reeds appeared even darker. "Let's go back, we can't see clearly." My cousin seemed tired and urged me to go back, so we left the clumps of reeds. Ah! The fish basket was really heavy. I couldn't walk as fast as when I came! The fish, big and small, were jumping around in the net. The basket on my back was a bit uneasy. It was hard to find my way home.

But, the next day, those jumping fish, ah, had already been stiffly burned to death in the pot! You poor fish! People's laughter is built on your deaths! At this time, I suddenly thought of our current China, our current China is like the fish on the line of death!
