Short News

Recent News from Meihua Girls' High School

Meihua Girls' High School at No. 61 Kade Road has been practical and realistic in everything since its establishment. Recently, it has increased the purchase of books and added various specimens of animals and plants, making the facilities even more complete. In terms of sports, a basketball court has also been added for serious training, so that students can get in-depth training in physical education.

Good News for Learning Esperanto

Esperanto has been introduced to China for more than twenty years. Since the establishment of the Shanghai Esperanto Association (now in Yongping Lane, Kade Road), the number of students has increased dramatically in the past three years due to the association's active promotion. It has held many training courses, cultivating nearly a thousand Esperanto talents. It is now heard that the eleventh session has started last Tuesday evening, and there are still some vacancies. Those who are interested in learning can contact the association. It is also learned that the association traveled to Suzhou during the spring vacation, and many people participated.

Vocal Basic Exercises Published The new curriculum standards for junior high school music recently promulgated by the Ministry of Education stipulate that more than ten minutes of pronunciation exercises must be conducted before teaching singing, but this standard has not been sold in the market for a long time since its promulgation. Mr. Qiu Menghen, a giant in the music industry in this city, has compiled a book of vocal music basic exercises based on his ten years of teaching experience and based on this standard. The teaching materials are sufficient for the three academic years of junior high school, and the teaching methods are explained in detail in the examples. It is a good textbook for junior high school music lessons. It has now been published and sold by Kaiming Bookstore on Simalu Road, Shanghai. The price is only 25 cents per copy. The Chengzhong, Lida, Aiguo, Xinmin, Guangdongdong; Fushi, Shangzhong, Ji Shi, Dazhong, Minzhi, Huzhong, and Hangzhou Jinan Suzhou and other middle schools in this city have all adopted this book.

Literary Works

Decline (1)

— Shen Qianli

It only takes a day to get from Shanghai to my hometown; there are trains and ships to take, and the road is not lonely. In terms of convenient transportation, it is indeed worthy of my gratitude. The day I arrived home was the evening when the rural customs were busy with "sending off the stove god." If it were today five years ago, the whole village would have been filled with a festive mood. However, what was reflected in my eyes on this day was only a dead village; in front of every earthen brick wall, there was a quiet and desolate scene.

The piercing north wind pushed the fallen leaves on the ground, swirling in the open space of the rice threshing ground, making a rustling sound like water泻. My porter and I walked silently, and hearing that kind of reverberating sound of leaves, I couldn't help but think that this was a harbinger of a decline in the countryside!

From the wharf to my home, there was a distance of three miles. My porter and I walked in this hazy night. We passed through more than a dozen villages in the middle, and each village showed a decadent appearance like anemia. Finally, we stepped on the edge of our village; the village where I grew up and haven't seen for five years, everything I saw at this time was only more extraordinarily old!

The entire village was immersed in the dark night, and for a moment, I couldn't find my own home; my porter and I groped around the village, and only by using the power of lighting match after match, could we recognize that there was a stone for tethering cattle at the gate of my house!

A few hours of running around reduced my strength to talk when meeting family members!

"Young master! Young master! Why are you back so late?" The servant Afu opened the door. Suddenly seeing my unfamiliar face that he hadn't seen for several years, he didn't dare to believe that I would come back at this time; he used the light emitted from the house, opened his eyes, and carefully looked around on my face for a while, before shouting at me the title he had shouted at me a few years ago.

"Hmm! Help me take the things in, Afu!" Extreme exhaustion made me only coldly perfunctorily deal with Afu's excited expression.

"Young master! You go inside first. I'll move these things." He still greeted me so warmly.

"Okay, no rush; are they all in the back?" Afu's enthusiastic touch made me understand that this time I couldn't help but speak in this environment.

Afu moved the things into the hall one by one, and without even breathing a sigh, he rushed ahead of me to the back, still chanting urgently in his mouth: "Young master is back! Young master is back!"

Hearing Afu's enthusiastic shouting, I couldn't help but feel a burst of shame in my heart!

The family members were all led out by Afu's shouting; the doorway of the "ancestral hall" was crowded with many gloomy faces of men and women, but when our lines of sight met, a kind of indescribable smile was piled on each face. Looking at the family's warm welcoming mood, I couldn't think of a single beautiful word to give them some comfort!

The "ancestral hall" was cold and ordinary, and none of the things that should have been placed during the New Year were placed at this time. A thick cobweb was hanging on the "insurance lamp" hanging in the middle of the hall, swinging in the air with the wind; I had just stepped into the "ancestral hall" and was stunned for a while by these many unpleasant scenes. The lively scene of five years ago unconsciously climbed into my heart again.

Seeing my strange behavior, the family members all just stood blankly in front of me, and no one seemed to have thought of what questions they should ask this unfamiliar person who had been away for five years. I turned around and glanced at them, and then I realized that one of the leading figures of my family was missing from this crowd.

"Where did Dad go? Why isn't he home yet, Mom?" I walked to my mother's side, stroking her shoulder and asking. I only saw that the black hair on her head had also turned into a pale color with the passing of time.

"He went to town, probably he'll be back soon? Haven't you eaten yet, Kun'er!" She forced a little smile on her face, and her hands frequently touched my face, her attitude seeming so unnatural.

When I asked these words, they all suddenly looked startled, and exchanged glances with each other in frustration. But in an instant, they all focused their gazes on my mother's face, and everyone stood there naturally with gray eyes, seemingly feeling a kind of panic that a misfortune was about to befall between my mother's opening of her lips.

"Isn't it going to be 'sending off the stove god' tonight? What did Dad go to town to do?"

Judging from the expressions on many people's faces, I guessed that my father's trip to town was definitely not as simple as my mother said.

"Yes, he went to town to buy things for 'sending off the stove god.' Kun'er! You eat first, and Dad will be back in a while." My mother glanced at them, and then shouted: "Afu—go tell Third Aunt to get food for the young master!"

The wrinkles on my mother's forehead were piled up thickly like the folded canvas on a boat, and a wave of doubt shifted on those deep wrinkles; but she still looked at me with so much pretense of calmness, seemingly wanting to find a little comfort in this face of mine that had been taken away from the childhood plumpness by the wandering life.

Opening Chapter "Courtship"

The sun sets on Coal Mountain, is there a shadow or not. A beautiful girl admires herself in the mirror, tidying her hair. Suddenly in the mirror, she sees her lover arrive. With delicate fingers, she arranges her temples. She stands up and puts down the comb. Hastily, she pulls on her sleeve. She calls out "Brother, please sit down. Sit beside me and keep me company. Why haven't you come lately? I suspect you have a beautiful girl elsewhere." The lover listens and rubs his hands. "I thought you women were too talkative. Last time I wanted to see you, but there were too many sisters in your house. I previously asked for your birth date, but your father didn't agree. What to do? Today I received a letter from the study. Your father is sending you away to marry another. It scared me to death!" "Miss, fate is determined from a past life. If we don't have the blessing in this life, then let it be. I can only shave my head and chant Amitabha." The lady listens and laughs, "You have wasted your studies; you have no talent. Wait until I get married, and come visit me before the full moon. If my husband asks who you are, just call yourself a cousin. And I will call you cousin."

Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

Madge Evans Dislikes Her Acting Ability Being Too Broad

— Fu

According to the current star system, an individual's success largely depends on the development of his personality. The expression of his personality, now on the screen, is what is commonly known as style. Once a movie star's style has become unique and recognized by the audience, it is often difficult to change. Therefore, apart from many established stars who already enjoy a unique status through their unique style, many aspiring but not yet famous actors are most afraid of being classified into a certain style or category. This is probably because once categorized, job opportunities become fewer and the path to success narrows.

This is the general sentiment of ordinary film actors. They do not want to be placed in a narrow category. They want to be called versatile geniuses. They like to hear people praise them as versatile actors. However, for the sake of exploring the film industry, we must introduce a female actor who is known as versatile, but has been harmed by her versatility and continues to play secondary roles.

Madge Evans is also a very famous star. She has soft yellow hair, slightly golden, light blue eyes, and an extremely beautiful posture. She is a versatile actor who can do anything. In the past four years, she has acted in thirty-four films, and recently played the important role of Agnes in "David Copperfield," which can be considered a lot of work. However, she is still a secondary actor, although she is the best among the secondary ones.

Why? According to her own discovery, it is because her performance range is too broad, and it is too easy to play any role, so she has not yet been recognized by the film production authorities and the audience as belonging to which category. She dislikes her own versatility and would rather succeed in a unique style and show off her expertise.

Madge said: "An actress is usually limited and becomes a certain style. But when a certain style needs a certain actor, she is immediately selected. As a result, what she gets is recognition and success. For example, Garbo is limited by her figure (square shoulders), face (high cheekbones), and voice (coarse and hoarse), and has become a foreign style, suitable for performing mysterious and seductive girls. She occupies the top spot in this category, and no one can compete with her.

"The rest are also the same. Joan Crawford, Katharine Hepburn, Ann Harding, Constance Bennett, Mae West, they each have their own personality, expertise, style, and category, and they are not confused with each other. Whether in the eyes of producers or audiences, they are all unique and forever so. Therefore, when it comes to the most important role casting, their suitability and ability have long been recognized by the directors, and they naturally assign important roles to them.

"But what about me? The remaining inconspicuous, meaningless roles have my name written on them. They know that I can do anything and look like anything. So whether it is the daughter of a physical education teacher in a football film, a British noblewoman in a social film, a female entrepreneur in New York, or a Chinese nanny, when they lack suitable actors, it is my opportunity to perform. I have been playing random roles for a long time now. To keep myself from being too disappointed, I would rather break this environment and be recognized by people in a certain style."

This broad acting ability was initially a welcome asset, but it gradually made her tired. However, a genius like Madge Evans probably won't let her be disappointed in the end, right?

Review of "The Fugitive"—Jin Cheng

— Ling He

In today's era when upright gentlemen lament the decline of national spirit, "The Fugitive," which appears with a positive anti-imperialist and anti-Japanese stance, is being released at this time, which seems to be a cup of bitter wine for the vast audience deeply mired in national destruction and family ruin. This bitter wine makes people cry and shed tears, and at the same time makes people roar with boiling blood.

After watching it, this film is written like this: In the poor and peaceful northern border region, the planes of imperialists cruelly bombed their hometown. Their parents, children, were sacrificed under the bloodbath, so the survivors fled with the old and the young. In the vast and boundless desert, in hunger, thirst and wind and sand, they struggled on the line of death. Flee, flee painfully and cry out, but where is their hometown? Where is their home? They died under the imperialist bombs, and also died from hunger, thirst and disease. However, rich young masters took the opportunity to abduct homeless girls, and some cunning profiteers buried greedy old men in the desert in order to sell people, while the girls were transferred to the hands of lustful perverts. At the same time, on the other hand, there were so-called big-bellied capitalist philanthropists, who profited from the good name of sheltering refugees, indulging in their own enjoyment of embezzling donations, while the refugees got thin porridge that they could not eat enough of, and slept in dirty hard houses, making the young masters smell the unpleasant stench. They groaned and endured in a life of whipping and cursing, until they could no longer endure it, they finally roared! They finally recognized who their greatest enemy was. In order to recover their lost land, to return to their hometown, and to escape from the line of death and struggle to survive, they used agricultural tools such as hoes as weapons. In the majestic marching music, they shouted slogans to recover the lost land and made the final fight against imperialism. As mentioned above, "The Fugitive" has its great significance when it is released at present.

Yes, the screenwriter's intentions are good. He dares not go with the flow of singing and dancing for peace, and he has not forgotten that the Chinese people are in a national crisis of dire straits. With the greatest enthusiasm for national salvation, he uses film art to arouse the ambition of the common people to resist, to restore the broken mountains and rivers through effective national war, and to seize the existence of the free position of the Chinese nation. However, in terms of creative methods, this is not a perfect artistic work. At least in terms of performance techniques, there are still many places that deserve to be brought up and discussed with the screenwriters and directors. At the same time, there are also many excellent scenes that are worth mentioning to introduce to the audience.

What moves us the most is that the author tightly grasps the audience's sad emotions with cruel depictions. He made Qin Tong buried in the sand, only showing his head and neck. We have seen the same scene of burying serfs alive in Eisenstein's "Storm Over Mexico" and were greatly moved by it. Now that Qin Tong is buried in the desert, although the author did not explicitly tell us whether he was buried alive or buried after death, the degree of cruelty deeply stimulates the audience's hearts. Similarly, in the refugee shelter, the refugees who could not grab porridge to eat were also whipped. As for the various escapes in the desert, the death of Shao Ying's uncle, the injury of his father, and Shao Ying's burial of the young girl left behind by his uncle, all made the audience shed tears sadly.

Perhaps some people feel that the scenery of the northern border is not described sadly and desolate enough, but the pastoral mood at the beginning, the wailing of the sheep, the sad flute sound, the gray sky and the desolate land, are somewhat like lyrical poems. As for the vast desert, with wind and sand blowing, and the refugees suffering from hunger and thirst, this deep sadness, compared with the bitter rain and cold wind in the south, is a completely different kind of bitterness.

In "Rage of the China Sea," we have already appreciated the author's quite powerful performance of mass scenes. Similarly, the bombing by the imperialist planes, the fire, the shouts and running of the masses, which are the highlights of the play here, are even more powerful when compared with the bustling worship of gods that immediately follows. As for the fight scene later, it is also passable.

But at the same time, there are also many shortcomings. The most important thing is that in terms of screenwriting methods, it is impossible to gradually improve the activity of this group of anti-imperialist resistance, and we even only see the bloodbath of imperialism, but do not see any expression of their intuitive hatred for the enemy. Therefore, the anti-Japanese war led by Shao Ying later only felt like a sudden and reluctant tail added on. In fact, the refugees' anti-Japanese war is a decided way out, but the author avoids the important and takes the light and cannot grasp the inevitable process.

Another major shortcoming is the poor understanding of weaving methods in the directorial method. We see that many places are not connected. It is almost taking care of one thing and losing the other, writing the stories separately, and not being able to weave them together intricately. Naturally, it also contains many screenwriting errors; such as Xiao Yun's mistaken entry into the young master's house and Shao Ying's finding her, are both coincidental uses. As the Shao Ying siblings did not know that the third girl was also in the room, they actually uncovered her quilt in a tense scene, and even the process of the third girl's suicide all prove that the director's handling was inappropriate. Although these are all shortcomings of the script, the director is not unable to remedy them.

What I want to say again is the author's tone for the whole play. Because the scenery of the northern border uses too few long shots, (such as Yuan Meiyun's singing is always a panning shot.), so that it cannot give us a deeper sense of desolation. Sometimes the tone of the play is too slow, especially some panning shots are too slow, which makes people feel stagnant and dull. As for inserting extremely slow caressing of corpses and painful crying into the air of fighting, it certainly destroys the tense air.

People may be moved by the activeness of its theme, and feel that these technical details do not need to be demanding, but with good intentions, but not being able to express them more skillfully and deeply, this makes the activeness of the content also lose its great social value; although the form is not enough to express the content, it is a common problem of China's emerging films. However, we will not ignore the difficulties in creating the environment for Chinese films. The most obvious thing is to replace the words "Japanese imperialism" with "them," which shows the author's painstaking effort to avoid the important and take the light.

The acting, set design, and songs all have better results, but the dubbing has not yet been selected to a perfect level. Due to space limitations, other details are omitted.

Review of "The Gilded Lily"

— Ji Han

The Gilded Lily—Grand Theater Screening

Continuing the current most popular style of American films, "The Gilded Lily" fully expresses the light and humorous mood. It gives us pleasure from beginning to end, and deeply portrays the personality of the characters in the play in this lightness and humor. For example, the male protagonist Pete is so unruly and unrestrained that he must take off his shoes in the park, and sometimes forgets to wear shoes and walks barefoot on the ground. This kind of place makes people laugh, and at the same time feel that he has a lovely personality. Similarly, the female protagonist Marilyn, the first time she sang and danced in a nightclub, she forgot the lyrics, she felt very embarrassed, but she was very humorous and witty, and cleverly supported the embarrassing situation. Of course, she is not mischievous, but it gives you a very innocent and lovely impression. These places show the ingenuity of the director or actors, and more importantly, the youthful and lively charm of the screenwriter, as the basis for success.

Furthermore, the screenwriter is very experienced and has a cold-eyed philosophy of life, which is used as a positive transmission on the male protagonist. He is very satisfied with his profession, does not desire or demand too much, sits quietly in the park with his lover on Thursday to eat plums and talk casually, enjoying himself. Even when proposing to his lover, he is not reluctant. If they can get married, they will get married, otherwise, it doesn't matter if they wait for a while, he doesn't care. But he understands that women are not easy to completely get rid of the desire to improve their lives, and even make him lose love. But this cannot be forced, it is better to let it develop naturally. So when he knew that his lover was admiring the son of an English earl, although he had jealousy, he did not throw the photo of his rival on the ground twice? He still shrugged and put it back in place. Not only that, he was also happy to accompany his lover to visit his rival (the earl's son). Until the lover realized that the young master did not have true love for her, he did wait for her to return to him.

However, this is only a love comedy, and apart from the portrayal of love, there is no more important reflection of reality. We are not demanding at all; for example, in the United States, which is extremely trapped in social chaos and unemployment panic, the male and female protagonists would never be as settled and happy as the screenwriter wrote, right? This cannot but be a whitewash of consciousness.

Yes, here I just want to create a light comedy. In order to obtain a graceful and sweet mood, both the director and the actors are more than competent. Perhaps it can be said that Wesley Ruggles will not have the humor of Lubitsch or Capra, "The Gay Divorcee" or "Midnight," but Wesley Ruggles is by no means a failure. For example, when Marilyn suddenly bid farewell to the earl's son in England and packed up to return to China, those reporters were quickly taking pictures, which can prove his quickness. But when Marilyn and the earl's son are talking about love on the beach, the bare feet that come and go as a moving background are too many, and become a minor flaw. Claudette Colbert's acting skills are best displayed in this kind of light film, and it seems to be far above those ancient palace films. As for the male lead, he is naturally also very successful.

Movie novel

The Hate of a Fallen Indian Nation (Clive of India) (8)

— Mao De

Clive said, "But, my dear, our money is all gone. We don't have a single penny." Margaret heard her husband's words and, although startled, felt even more distressed, but she comforted him, saying, "But we still have each other, don't we?" As she spoke, she suddenly noticed a change in his expression and asked in alarm, "What's wrong?" Clive shifted uneasily, and after a moment said, "A blessing in disguise is that just as this bad news arrived, the East India Company sent someone to invite me to go. They want me to go to India again. Imagine!"

Margaret asked eagerly, "And then?" Clive said, "I have to leave tomorrow. It's extremely urgent. After tomorrow, I'll have to wait several weeks for another ship." After he finished speaking, the two fell silent, their thoughts surging, and they couldn't speak for a moment. Margaret felt a powerful force that, after uniting them as husband and wife for several years, was now about to tear them apart, and even take their son away. Although she appeared calm, her heart was in utter disarray, but she tried her best to think about which path was best.

When Clive spoke, he naturally hoped that Margaret would go with him. She thought that if she accompanied her husband to India, they were both young, Clive was only twenty-five, and after a few years they would still return to England. At that time, everything would surely be restored to its former glory, houses, children, money, endless happiness. But she also thought that no matter how rich and honorable they became in the future, their first beautiful dream had already vanished. They could have children in the future, but their current child would never return.

Thinking of this, she couldn't help but feel grief. She felt that she absolutely could not follow her husband to India. She had to stay with her son until he died. She wanted to cherish the remaining unfulfilled dream in her heart, even though she knew it couldn't last long. Finally, she made up her mind and told him Lord Ferris's words. Clive was stunned for a long time after hearing this, staring at Margaret's face. He then asked, "Really? Really… is there no hope at all?" When Margaret remained silent, only lowering her head, he also whispered, "Child…" and couldn't say another word.

After a while, Clive finally spoke, "Don't remember what I said. Of course, you can only stay here. In a mother's heart, of course, her son comes first." He stood up and walked to the upstairs nursery, which Clive had specially decorated for his son. He asked, "Can I see him now?" Margaret nodded. Clive said again, "Go and tell the servants to pack my luggage." With that, he went upstairs.

Margaret called the housekeeper, Miss Cripps, and instructed her to pack Clive's luggage. As she was about to leave, Margaret stopped her again. Miss Cripps hurried back, but Margaret was silent for a long time, unable to speak. Finally, she said, "Pack my things too, and put them together. I'll come up and help you in a bit." Miss Cripps couldn't help but wonder, "But… madam… what about the child…"

Margaret quickly stopped her, "Never mind! Pack the luggage! I'm telling you to pack the luggage! Pack the luggage!" Miss Cripps, seeing the miserable and impatient look of her mistress, silently retreated. After Miss Cripps left, Margaret thought that no matter what, she had to accompany her husband to India. Her son could be cared for by servants and treated by specialists until he passed away, but her husband had no one to comfort him or discuss matters with except her. (To be continued)
